O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, my dearest son, I have completed this book which is the last of the medical science together with its fulfillment, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came upon me to envision that I would complete it with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely 'surgery'.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is much neglected in our region and has been entirely suppressed everywhere, the science has therefore perished and its strength lies only in the small descriptions found in books which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and the science is ignored.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I wish to revive it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of the iron tools for cauterization, and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And therefore, whoever engages in this must rise to the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and how they move and remain at rest, and where their exit points are located.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates said that the name without work is worth little, but with work it is much; and likewise in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that anyone who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before should be careful lest they fall into error and kill people, as I have seen many times those who engage in this science without abandoning their ignorance and inexperience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut off one aposteme of scrofula from the neck of a woman and cut the arteries of her neck; so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another doctor who removed a stone from the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; so he took away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called for to remove it, and saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they tried to cut into him he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another doctor who took in charge one duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breaking had a wound. And the doctor, full of ignorance, tied the break above the wound with straps so tight that he did not leave any calamine on the wound, and left him like that for one day. And he ordered that it should not be untied, and thus the leg became entirely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come unbind his leg; and when I untied it, he felt at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But the corruption was already well established in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the member until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who burst an inflamed aposteme and then set it on fire through the wickedness of his ignorance.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is free from melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all that is corrupted can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that the art of hands is divided into two parts: namely, work where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because it is necessary that you guard yourself so that foolish doctors cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your weapons in haste and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way, then through God's grace you will come to salvation and be praised; and leave fearful diseases to those of harsh healing; and put away your weapons from those who cause you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on serious illnesses unless you wish to be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medicated cauteries. It is arranged from the head down to the feet. It discusses the shapes of instruments, the irons for cauteries, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, cupping glasses and wounds, extracting splinters, and similar things. It is arranged with the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter concerns restoring dislocations and distortions, as well as similar matters. It is arranged from the head to the feet with the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we begin discussing the work, it is necessary for me to describe the quality of each temperament and its benefit or harm.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of benefit and harm are lengthy discussions and subtle sciences, involving secret responses. Many wise men have spoken about this topic and agreed upon it. However, they allowed me few words because I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery universally benefits every temperament where it has material, except for two temperaments: the hot and dry without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	Regarding the hot and dry temperament with matter, some people argue that cautery is greatly beneficial there, while others claim the opposite, saying that cautery is not useful for illnesses caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness. But those who argue otherwise say that cautery provides great benefit for hot and dry illnesses found in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body and moisture of man to the temperament of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And let no one meddle with this matter except those who have proven it and know well the chapter on cautery and the diversity of temperaments in men, as well as the dispositions, causes of their illnesses, seasons, and ages. We are not afraid for other temperaments, especially for cold and moist ones.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians agreed upon the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, son: cautery along with fire is one of the secrets of cure and has greater benefit than cauterizing with burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not harm any other member if it is applied to the one being cauterized, except for those that are named otherwise.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot remedies pass from one member to another, causing serious illnesses in the limbs; but sometimes fire, due to its strength and virtue, does not act unless there is an excess of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experience and the length of service and study that I have devoted to this art, which is based on truth. Therefore, I apologize for the length of my words, as it does not please me to hide from you the secret contained in fire and its ability to overcome illnesses in bodies, as philosophers demonstrate; now receive these thoughts into your mind.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	"And know, son, that they agreed upon when cauteries ought to be performed, and chose priests."
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	"And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harm happening underneath is diminished with the aid of the cautery; and especially if cauteries are necessary for sudden and severe pains which cannot wait until greater injury comes to the limb."
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	"And do not think, dear son, as foolish physicians sometimes do; for the disease that is cured by cautery has no recurrence. They say so indeed; but it is not entirely true, because cauteries are medicines which change the complexion and dry up the humors causing pain, and they act more quickly than other medicines in their strength and power."
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	"And it is possible that sometimes the disease may come according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease itself in its power. The excess humors are collected there through consumption of foods and similar things except when cauteries are applied where there is little excess or moisture, such as those for toothache and similar ailments, and then such pain does not return; but this happens rarely."
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	"And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and indeed it is so; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth trying after medicines have failed, their intentions are mistaken, for when we have tried various remedies for a disease and they do not work, then we apply cauteries, and they are effective."
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	"So it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, but not according to the intentions of foolish physicians."
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	"The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are more beneficial than those made of iron, and they said this only because of the quality and nobility of gold. They also said that the place where a cautery is applied does not cause corruption, but this is not true, as I have proven it myself; for in some people it does cause corruption. And yet, cauteries made of gold are more beneficial than those made of iron, just as they said."
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	"And besides, when you heat an instrument made of gold, you cannot tell exactly when it is hot because of the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly. And if it is heated too much, it melts in the fire, so there are many drawbacks to using them."
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	"And for these reasons we use iron cauteries that we have better adapted to our work."
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	"Now I have arranged this chapter from beginning to end so that it may be easier to find."
dou cautere olivaire	"about the olive cautery"
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	"This cautery is beneficial for moistness and coldness on the head, and there are two kinds of it that are made because of an illness called 'sodicity' and because of many humors descending from the head to the eyes and ears, and for excessive sleepiness, toothache, sore throat, and especially all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, sciatica, apoplexy, and similar illnesses."
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	"The shape of this cautery is as follows: the patient should be purged with a soluble and moisturizing medicine for three nights or four, according to what the virtues and age and habits of the patient can tolerate. Then perform the cautery on the head of the patient."
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	"And then have the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, with their hands on their knees. Then place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two eyes; where your middle fingers will meet is where you should make the incision, and then heat the cautery called 'olive,' which has this shape:"
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And place the cautery on the marked spot, and move it downwards and outwards little by little while turning your hand. Then lift your hand gently, and examine the area to see if you can see a small piece of bone; if not, continue with the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. Then take a little piece of wool, soften it in warm water, put it on a cotton pad, place it on the area, and leave it for three days. After that, apply a compress made of linen soaked in butter; leave it there until the inflammation has healed. Then treat the wound with the ointment called 'tetrafarmacon' until it is completely healed."
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	"And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges itself. And for this reason, it helps to leave it open longer."
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	"And some of these people say that one should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone and heal it."
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	"And others say that one should leave the cautery on until it burns down to the bone as large as a thread used by women for spinning, so that the humors can flow out more easily. Then one should leave the wound open for a long time before healing and dressing it."
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	"And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in all respects, except perhaps in some cases where there is a need for fear. But I think that it is better to leave the cautery alone; because the flesh is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we can see in other members; and even when the flesh of the patient is naturally weak, the first indication of cauterization is more salutary and beneficial for me, and this is the method that I generally use."
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	"about chronic headache"
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	"If a patient has chronic pain in the whole head that lasts for a long time, they should use diuretics and pills called 'cochiae,' and remedies for purging the head, oils, and plasters. And if one applies the cautery I mentioned earlier, it will not be beneficial."
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	"Be careful if the patient's flesh is of strong nature and not too cold; in this case, you may cauterize them with the cautery that we mentioned earlier."
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	"Afterwards make the cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery at the point called 'vessels,' which is where cupping glasses are placed. And do not press your hand too hard so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak about it elsewhere. And the cauteries on the horns must be finer than those used for the middle of the head, and here is the shape:"
dou cautere dou chief	"about the cautery of the head"
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of medicine are such that you take one stalk of mallow, remove the skin and cut it into two pieces at the roots, then make a hole in the temple where the pain holds in such a manner that you can place the stalk of mallow beneath the skin; and when it has been placed so, tie it tightly and leave it thus for twelve hours; then untie it and draw out the stalk of mallow, leaving the wound thus for two or three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter until it comes out of its own accord.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until it is healed, and if you see that some burning medicines are needed, then refer to the twelfth treatise on burning medicines which I have written.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery should be applied in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron from which this shape is made:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a hook, with a little curve at its end and a small opening in the middle. It is placed on the painful spot and you hold your hand while slightly turning the iron so that half of the surface of the heart-shaped tip gets burned; then lift your hand so that the artery does not get burnt, which lies outside, and allow plenty of blood to flow out abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward put cotton on wool and place it on the spot for three days; then I put moistened cotton in butter, and afterward heal the spot with ointment until it is clean; and if you wish to cauterize this ulcer with the cautery called 'cultellare', do so at its tip, being careful not to touch the artery in this ulcer which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of ulcer
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat an ulcer as we have previously described in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries mentioned earlier with medicine and iron do not suffice for it, then you must heat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it is white; and seize beforehand on the spot a line half the length of two fingers, and remove your hand once, ensuring that you do not touch the artery and that you do not reach the bone; and beware of the mandible which moves when chewing, and ensure that the nerve has no regard for the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the loss of blood from the artery when it is cut or when cutting causes great fear, especially to those who are not skilled and experienced; and leave the work in mid-course; but I will tell you how one restrains blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and heal the wound until it is clean; and if you wish, administer the cautery which we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	For pain in the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold pain comes to the ear, and one has opened there medications dissolving and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have made a full circle around the sick ear, or around the two if the pain is in both of them, and then move it away from the root of the ear where you have marked the location, and there are ten points around each ear; afterwards cure the place until it is clean.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Tortures that must be cured by cautery are only those that move with phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cauteries on those that come from scorching or inflammation of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you are curing this type of torture that moves with phlegm from hydres and purgations of the head and gargarisings, and these do not help, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the sick person with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another a little bit outside the temple, and the third in the meeting of the two lips; and put the cautery in the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery against the head of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple just as long as a finger; and leave the cautery there until half of the kernel is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the likeness of the cautery that we have placed before, but it is a little more delicate and the knife must be a little thicker; afterwards cure the place as I have said before, until it is clean.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you are curing it as we have said, but it does not help, and the sick person does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the place that is called "vessels" as we have said before, and behind the cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and it should be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is necessary to give the sick person large syrups and mondifying pills for the brain; afterwards raise the head of the sick person all the way up, and place on the occiput the plaster of mustard that is written about in the treatise of plasters; and this is the manner of cauterizing: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is cured thus, good; and if it is not, make three cauteries in the middle of the head going down to the neck, with a space of two fingers between each cautery; and cure it as the others, and if you see that they are stuck together, and the sick person is suffering, then make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, make two others on the two horns, and cure until it is healthy; and let the cauteries be those called "olivary", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed with syrups and other things that we have said before; afterwards raise the head of the sick person, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the sick person is suffering, and the disease is severe, then make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until half of the kernel is burned, and lift your hand; afterwards cure until it is healthy, and let the cauteries be those called "olivary" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epilithic should only apply fire cautery to those who are phlegmatic. First, one must modify the brain with herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in previous sections when the patient is large and able to tolerate medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is a child who cannot tolerate this treatment, one should perform gargarisings and mastications to modify the brain frequently with good meats. Afterwards, one should raise the head in the middle and apply one cautery according to what we have said before, and one cautery on the vessel and each horn; and if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, one should apply cauteries as I have described for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, using olive oil according to the method I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, one should apply a single subtle cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the excesses or corrupted moisture are caused by melancholy and produce thick phlegm, then apply as many cauteries as we have described for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the excess is inclined towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist due to melancholy, then give them something to drink that cleanses the brain according to what is written earlier in this section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, raise the head of the patient. Next, make one torch of well-woven linen in the shape of a circle and place it on the head. Have the patient sit crossed-legged and hold them tightly on all sides. Then present the liniment made with melted sheep's wool fat that has been warmed gradually over fire so that the patient can tolerate it when poured onto their forehead. Afterwards, remove the circle from inside the head and let it cool. Do this to the patient once a week along with other good treatments until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize wounds by making several pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery increases moisture in the brain; then put cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	Here begins a chapter on the eye.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it first comes to the eyes as described in the division by signs I've mentioned, then begin and give the patient something purifying the head, keeping away all moistures, and make them sweat or take many baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After commanding him to raise his head, and make a cautery within the head, and make two cauteries upon the two temples if the descent of the eye is in two eyes together, or one if the descent is in one; and cut away all veins and arteries that are under the heart with the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the breadth of the temple; and take care that there is no shedding of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incising the cautery how you should stop it; and sometimes one makes a cautery or incision under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	Regarding the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and customary and are upon the veins or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside, and it is seen that they are cold superfluities of phlegm, then make the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of the eye descending into the eyes: one cautery within the head, and two cauteries upon the two temples, and two cauteries or incisions under the two bones behind; and if there is need for more, then cauterize gently above the eyebrow with many small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Regarding the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you have treated it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then let him drink three nights running of raw onions; afterwards raise his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the cautery called "olivary"; and make two cauteries with the cautery called "clavilis" upon the two eyebrows, a little below the eyebrows; and take care that you do not cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When paper made from oil is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the shape
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see fit, make two cauteries upon the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not leave your hand there except until about a third of the paper is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Regarding the eyelashes that touch the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned towards the inside and touch the eye, causing harm. In this case, one makes cauteries in two ways: either with fire or with a burning medication.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Where fire cauterization is ordered for the patient, let them keep their hairs long and even. If they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Once the hairs have grown and are even, then place the patient on their back. Next, draw a figure onto paper that is similar to the shape of the palm of your hand, with the beginning of the mark near the hairs; then put moist cotton in egg white and musk mallow on the eye, and then heat the cauterizing iron that has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize the drawn figure little by little many times until the skin is burnt there. The sign of the work's healthiness is that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs lift at the point of the eye. Then remove your hand, and leave it like this for three days, after which put moist cotton in butter until the burn is healed; afterwards anoint it until it is sound.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come back, and the skin is softened, then begin the cauterization again on that same spot as you did at first. If the hairs are missing, cauterize it until the paper returns to its natural position, and becomes even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauterizing iron for medical use is made by ordering the patient to let their hairs grow long and even. Then make a shape out of parchment like the leaf of a myrtle tree. Next, take three parts each of French soap and live wax, grind them well together, and do it quickly so that it does not cool. Then spread it onto the shape you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it on the paper over the eyes. If the disease is only in one eye, then work on one; if it is in both, then do both. Put moist cotton in egg yolk under the eye. Have the patient lie on their back, and place your two fingers on top of the medicine, pressing gently once or twice whenever the patient feels a biting sensation from the medicine, for they will feel a biting sensation like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, then remove the medicine with your fingers.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the biting sensation has passed, then lift the eye-lid and see if you can raise the paper just as if it were lifted by heat or by cutting; and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply the medicine again on the eye where it has not opened until your efforts are equal and your eyes are at rest; then put cotton soaked in butter until the heat of the heart is extinguished, afterwards wash the eye with ointment called "diaphoresis" and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must guard your work carefully, so that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes moist and hairs prick in the eye, then restart the cautery on that softened area with clean paper, just as you did before; afterwards continue the treatment until it is healed; this is the form of the poultice for the wound:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this vary your constraints; and do not reply that which is right for you who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Here is the treatment for fistula by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in our divisions of diseases, but your treatment does not help,
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	"Instruct the patient to place their head in your hand; and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or turn its head. Afterward, place damp cotton in egg white or in juice of parsley on the eye; afterward heat the cautery which is shaped thus: and it should be raised at the head like the form of a pigeon's feather, together with which should be the cautery; if you wish, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, it should also be like a tent; but nonetheless, this which is raised is useful for your work."
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	"Afterward press the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus from it, and dry it. And if it is closed, open it, and draw out the bowels. Afterward place the hot cautery on it, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part of the nail above the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and burn it."
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then restart the cautery once more, and if necessary, do so again, leaving it for three days; afterwards apply moist cotton in butter, and continue the treatment with a drying ointment until healed. If it is not healed after forty days, apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is another manner of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand, make a fistula, then cut open its location. Afterward, insert cannula of fine copper here; this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	"And they make it to the quantity of three drops of lead; and hold your hand on the reed firmly, and do not let the patient move his head at all, so that the melted lead does not run into his eye; and it is necessary to place damp cotton in egg white or in wax on the eye of the sick person: the lead thus burns the place of the fistula, and heals it by wonderful healing."
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must administer a probe to the nose and bring the fistula back to its proper place in the body of the nose.
des crevaices en levres	"for cracks in lips"
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks occur on lips which are called "hairs", especially on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks which we have mentioned in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat up a small cautery scalpel according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly in those cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, clean the area with wax until it is smooth.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil on the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When a boil comes on the root of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and it becomes putrid and reddened and forms a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, but it does not improve: then it is necessary for you to have an cautery according to the size of the fistula. Then heat the cautery at the opening or hole of the fistula, holding your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it and the surrounding area; do this once or twice, then treat it as we have said in treatments until it is healed. And if it is healed thus, that's good; but if not, then it is necessary to uncover the area and remove the rotted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	on the mobility of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums become softened by moisture and the teeth become mobile, and you treat it with medicines but they do not help, then place the head of the patient on your lap. Afterwards, heat the cautery which will be described below in this manner: place a tube over the tooth; put the hot cautery inside quickly, holding your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth. Then remove your hand and recommence the cautery according to your desire. After that, have the patient rinse his mouth with salt water, keeping it in for an hour before spitting it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And thus the moving tooth is made firm, and the softened gum constrained, and corrupt moisture dried.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether it is hot or cold, and medical treatments are ineffective, then cautery should be used in two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is performed as follows: take some butter from a cow's udder and put it on the tip of an iron or brass spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the end of a needle, dip it into the melted butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth, holding it until it cools. Repeat this often so that its effects reach the root of the tooth. If you see that the cotton and wool become cold and hard with the butter, then place them on the aching tooth and hold a hot iron near the cheek until the heat reaches the base of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cauteries together are such that you should take a copper or bronze probe, and make it thick so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth. After heating the cautery, of which the form will come later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will be relieved the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then remove the heat; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	To perform cautery on any tooth you wish, according to your skill level, use this shape for the rod:
des scrophules	scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moistures, and is not responsive to digestion through medications, then use the cauterizing iron as described below, which has two openings for the smoke to exit from the other end; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, until it reaches the base of the abscess; if the abscess is small, use the cautery according to its size and leave it on for three days; afterwards, apply moistened cotton in butter until the scarring is healed; thereafter treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cauterizing iron:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moistures prevail upon the channels of the lung, especially when it is due to cold complexion, then the patient should first be treated with dissolving medicines. Afterwards, perform cauterization at the root of the throat, taking care not to come near the throat itself and not to burn too deeply into the chest.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let it be a cautery called "clavile," as we have shown its form before; and heal the place until it is sound.
de la toust	Here's how you can translate "de la toux" into English:
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of the lung are of cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or heat, and the disease is chronic, then perform two cauteries on the chest in close places; and one other cautery within the breast between the breasts; and let the cautery be called "clavile" according to the form that is mentioned above.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a cautery pricking all along the cautery called "poins," of which its form is shown here before, in the disease of the ears; and let there be about thirty points, or as many around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterward heal the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be of three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, perform them in three places.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the displacement of the shoulder joint
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder blade is dislocated due to moisture and is put back in place but cannot remain there and returns and dislocates again with even a small movement, as we have experienced it, then you must first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards have the patient lie on their back and side; then lift the heart which is inside the titillite with the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery that has 2 inches with this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the side, and let the figure of the cautery come together with four cauteries; and because this is done with the cautery that has 3 inches, therefore there are six cauteries for cauterization; and the nerves are according to the thinness of a thread, which is the form of the cautery that has 3 inches:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is joined onto this one nerve, so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards put on the cautery that has been crushed with salt; afterwards have the patient rest, and do not move their limbs for a long time until they are well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery clavile, or many cauteries pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is sound.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach so that they alter its nature, and catarrh is multiplied in it, and usual methods of treatment do not help, then the patient must be turned onto his back, extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this, make three fire cauteries: one below the armpit of the arm using the quantity of two fingers, for the entire cautery like a clove; and two cauteries in front of both sides such that the shape of the cauteries is at three angles, and there be enough space between one and another so they do not join together when they rot; and let the cauteries be so deep that they pierce both parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that it is necessary to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and whoever fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and pressing upon the stomach one point according to the quantity that you see fit; then cauterize for the entire cautery that is called "the point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment that we have discussed previously, let it be without wound.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver suffers pain from coldness and moisture and excess windiness, so much that it is greatly altered from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated for this as we have said in sections, but it does not benefit him at all, then the patient must be sounded on his hypochondrium; and there are three cauteries to be applied according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, avoiding the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come together; and let there be the thickness of two fingers between each cautery; and let the cauteries be long-bodied, and do not press too hard with your hand throughout the cautery; and let only half of the chest be burned, and let the patient stand upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms; this is the form.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if it is your wish, then cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all of the chest, for you would dry out the whole body; and do not let it come near the belly, for the heart is very subtle there, and especially so regarding this.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver,
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this treatment fails the physicians, so it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back; and then press firmly upon the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a razor, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the flesh is burned, and come up to the syphilis, until the pores are all open; after that treat according to the cure of the bones until it is healed; and it is not necessary that anyone but one who has studied medicine for a long time use this cautery, by whom many times these diseases have been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can boldly act, nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Regarding the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must perform cauteries for pleurisy with the roots of aristologia in this manner: take a root of aristologia that is long and as large as you can find, and let it be dry and also thick and long like your two fingers; and moisten it in oil, and heat it on the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the navel and the neck, and 2 small cauteries a little bit lower down in the part that is below the beard; and 2 cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning backwards a little bit; and one cautery inside the breast, and another on top of the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and 2 on each side of the breast away from the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand too hard, but rather do it openly as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient authors said that some people used a fire cautery resembling a razor, heated it and placed it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; and if pain occurs, as we have said in the case of the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this case, there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula occurs which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Regarding the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
