Then take a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe away blood, and use the spatula shaped like this:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is drawn from the temple to the second incision; and scrape away all the heart that is between the two slits up to the soft tissue that is on the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spongy material.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert the tool called "cultellarium" into the first slit, it is very sharp on one side and not sharp on the other side. This is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the thin blade towards the flesh near the heart, and the blunt blade towards the bone, and press until it reaches the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels descending from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to where the heart opens, and then do the same in the middle fissure up to the other end; and then extract blood evenly, and press the area for blood collection; then place a bandage of old cotton in each fissure, and cover with warm cloths soaked in wine and oil and rosewater, ensuring no abscesses form; and on the third day remove the ligature, and apply abundant cold water dressing, followed by basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until healed.
dou reume des eulz	This is an extract from "Le Grand Chirurgie" by Guy de Chauliac
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	If it happens that catarrh comes on suddenly, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakening of sight, and burned papers, and hair falling out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the sick person sneezes; then know by these signs that those matters and that catarrh come from many veins, and the cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And have the patient lie on their back, then make a long incision down the middle of the forehead, and another across its width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the crevice of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves near the temples that move during chewing; and when the bone is exposed, then suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then open between the two lips of the wound and put in old cotton and linen strips; then tie above it cloths dampened in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses; once they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that cause flesh to contract.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster out of it. And apply it to these wounds to encourage flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Chapter: "The Stopping of the Ears"
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When something like a stone falls into the ear or in some other manner that does not fit with the ear and does not grow within it, then place the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then bring about extraction; and when you sneeze with condimentum, and hold the nostrils closed when sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; then stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Fire cautery is often applied with this remedy; if it does not come to fire, then help should be sought through the use of subtle forceps. Here follows its form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with tweezers, that's good. If not, then extract with a fine, small hook; and if it does not come out with this, make a reed of straw and stick the end of the reed into the earhole hard, and stop what is around the reed with soft wax so that wind cannot enter with the reed; then blow fire strongly, for often fire comes thus as we have said; and if it does not come from fire in such manner, take glutinous substance which birds use, and put some of it on an instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glut on the stone or whatever thing it may be, and blow fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before inflammation and spasm comes, and the manner of cutting is thus: first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein according to his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small crescent-shaped incision in the root of the ear where it hangs; and let the incision be as large as you can get to the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and continue the treatment until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And help incise that boil.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this if you think that the boil is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many incisions. Then extract it with subtle forceps and suck out the pus, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, in the case of water entering the ear, the patient should first sneeze forcefully and plug the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it flows out by itself, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not [flow out], then take many pins according to the length of your thin fingers and light ones, and heat them slightly in fire. And have the patient insert one or two into their earhole, and stick it through on the other side with another pin; and keep doing this from pin to pin until all the water flows out, like this it will all flow out. If you see [the water], then take a straw, and put one end in the ear, and hold the other end over fire until the end of the straw is burnt. Then repeat with other straws until all the water flows out, as we have said earlier.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	"For the removal of the animal, if it is small-bodied like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division. But if it is large-bodied and can be felt, bring tweezers for its removal; this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear."
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	"For the removal of earthworms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the chapter on distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine tweezers; but if they are not visible, take the tube made of this shape:"
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Place the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck strongly on the whole cane; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey coming out, stop up around the cane with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not come out easily as we have said, administer distillations which the ancients have proved in the killing of worms, and you will find them treated in the writings on distillations; and thus distil your oils and medicines into the ear through all this instrument, of which here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	"And let it be made of silver or thin brass with a small hole below and wide above for distillation. And for pressing inside the distillation, use an instrument well-made for this purpose. And if you wish to take one razor and wrap cotton around its tip carefully; then pour your oil or juice into the tube along with whatever medicine you desire, and place the tube in the ear. Then insert the razor with all the cotton into the ear and press gently with your hand until the oil is distilled into the ear. And warm the patient's ear beforehand, and let the distillation be done in a small pot warmed over the fire before being distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not then be as effective."
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Chapter: "The Stopping of the Ears"
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and the same applies to adults due to injury or flesh grown inside the ear, which sometimes goes deep into the ear so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is one little opening that can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes deep inside so that it cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many cases. And in the case where there is an opening visible, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun and look inside: if you see any polyp appearing, then perform the operation described below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	"And let it be sharp and cutting both before and behind, full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the prolapse is of flesh born in the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is removed."
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operations are deeply embedded in the ear, then take a light and fine razor and heat it slightly on the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the operation where the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce gently, and be careful not to hurt the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Continue this process for several days until the wound is healed. Then take a gauze and moisten it in rose water, powdered vitriol, and apply it. If you see swelling of the ear, then remove the gauze and replace it with another gauze moistened in cerote made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling has gone down; then cure it until it is healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	"And if there is discharge of blood, take a sponge and wring it out in cold water, then place it on the ear. Use other remedies that stop the discharge of blood, which are found in treatises on distillations."
de la char des papieres	"What is written on the paper"
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	"This is the remedy that comes from paper of the eyes when they are moist and dried out. It is necessary to stretch them with tweezers and forceps, then cut it with a scalpel at its roots; then apply powdered vitriol."
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	"And if a thread of blood oozes out, then cauterize it with a lenticular cautery and cut it afterwards. This is more effective than cauterizing first. And often repeat this process until there is nothing left of its roots; for when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not grow back."
de la gresle	"Hailstorm"
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, hailstones come onto papers that appear like hail in shape and hardness, and therefore this disease is called "hail," which is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below. Its treatment is as follows: be aware if the hail moves from one side to another; it's easy to know; then make an incision wide, gently scrape each part, then grasp it with forceps, and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without slightly piercing the paper, it does not harm the patient. If the tear is large, gather it with a stitch and heal it until it is sound; if it is small, do not use force, for the ointment will restore it soon and form new flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	"And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over, and grasp the hail with tweezers and cut it on both sides; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the hail has been cut, rinse the wound with salt water, and heal it inwardly until the patient is healthy."
de la graisse des eulz	Here's a possible translation for "de la graisse des eulz":
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that enters the tissues of the papers above, which happens more in children than in adults. It greatly harms their eyes and causes them to have catarrh in the mornings, so they cannot look at the sunlight because tears rush into their eyes. Because of this, they often lie on their faces and sleep with their papers below their eyelashes moistened by the swelling and appearance covered with exinach that opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press hard with your two hands and feel the exit between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of removing it is as follows: the patient puts his head in your hand; then takes one linen cloth and prepares a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains eosinach from each part, then places it on top; and presses with his fingers on both sides so that the eosinach is gathered within the circle; then makes in the middle of the moistness with the sharp spatula a cut as wide as the wound made when bloodletting, and cuts the skin deeply until you reach the eosinach; and in several positions comes out eosinach from the cut, resembling the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take out with one piece of lint gripped between your fingers behind, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and make sure that you do not stuff in the cut, but wipe all the spatula up to the eye without cutting or hurting it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if eosinach does not come out at the beginning of the cut, then gently widen the cut a little until it appears; then remove it as we have said above, then moisten cloths in hot water and cold water, and place them on the wound, and press with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess forms, then treat it with poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hairs from the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs appear on the papers mixed with others than their natural ones and are entwined, they harm the eyes and cause diseases such as habitual tears, softening of the papers, and albugine, to such an extent that it causes destruction of the eyes. And there are four ways to treat it: either by cauterization with fire together or by hot medicine according to what is before or after cautery, and it can be done either by incision and suturing or by tweezers, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient's head in your hand, then turn the paper from the eye with your left hand; if it is folded over, that is good; if not, then insert a needle with one thread on top. And whether it is near the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing near those hairs, and pull one thread upwards along the entire length of the paper, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision underneath the paper, below the hairs attached, with the spatula cutting from the large pupil to the small one. Then remove one thread, and place a small tent made of cotton and cloth under the paper, then press on the paper in the shape of a cone, like a mortar pestle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the shape be according to the quantity that you see lifting up the paper which is divided into two parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need to cut a large quantity of paper according to how the paper has been softened; then make two lines on either side of where you have drawn with ink, and begin from the large artery up to the small one; and let one of the incisions be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the angles of the heart, then cut through all; then bring together the two lips with a stitch of thread made of fine wool, and absorb the blood, and cover the excess threads over both eyebrows with any sticky substance if you see fit to do so; and if not, pay no heed to it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching with dry and constricting substances, because the paper relieves at the joining of the wound and its gathering together, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is done without fear; and there is another method: and it is that you draw a figure on the paper similar to the shape of a laurel leaf as we have described, with three incisions made according to the shape that follows:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut that which is above the small forces equally according to the shape shown below:"
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you lack power to hold the tweezers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure; and place another thread beside the large artery, and the second thread beside the small one, and bring them together evenly between your two fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have cut, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar softening ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are turned: thus you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artistic.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	"The treatment of the canals is as follows: Convert the paper and make the slit within it according to what I have said, then make two fine canals by art equal in length to that of the paper and the width of the spatula; cut at both ends where you hold the threads. Then join one thread evenly onto that which lies above the paper of the eye, and strain both canals tightly from both parts; leave it thus for several days, and the skin that is strained will harden, darken, and shrivel until it adheres."
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, cut it with some force, then care for it until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, and the paper has been lifted off, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the shape of the two canals that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	"The operation is as follows: Take a fine needle and thread it with one thin, soft silk thread; then join the ends and tie them evenly, making the length of the threads a palm's breadth. Then take another short, fine silk thread and tie its end to the threads; then the patient should place his head in your hand, and be near the sun so that the operation may be clearly seen, for it is a delicate and subtle one. Then insert the needle throughout the canal into the root of the hair, joining it, and pierce it quickly through the paper until you draw it out above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the canal, and place it in the canal if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out of the canal into the paper with the natural hair."
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	"And if the canal is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the canal downward along all the thread that you have ordered, until the canal comes out of the hole above and you can see it through the vision of the eye; then pull out the canal and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and flesh grows over it. And if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long natural eyebrow hair, and raise it with that one which you leave, until it is separated and then lift it."
de la porriture de l’oil	"Treatment of eye inflammation"
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" occurs in the eye where corruption is present, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and another unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or cauterizing, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you cut through that scar, and separate the lips of it, and place linen wicks inside, and let it remain until it is healed; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but there are things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and rose water or white honey and linseed should be cooked, and ointments of diacylon melted in one of the oils, and wrapped in a wick, for its treatment.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your treatment are that you should take care that it does not heal in its former shape; and these works that we have mentioned serve only to prevent this illness from returning in its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that is underneath, which is truly called "axacrati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	An accident happens from wounding and cutting and cauterizing and similar things. The way of the operation in it is that you take a needle, on which there is doubled thread, and stick it into the flesh, making it pierce from the left eye to the right eye, so that the threads come out through two holes in the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the whole needle, and cut with one broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper comes back according to how it should be, that's good. But if not, then take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side within the paper; let the openings of the two cuts be at both angles of the incision you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are brought together, the figure is like the figure of a letter called "I Greek"; then remove that flesh according to how much its sides are beside it from what supports the paper, then join the two disjoined parts with a thread of wool; then follow the care that we have said about softening medicines and dressings until it's healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from cut or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make one full cut underneath the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage, as I have said; and one should do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters arrange various devices with all their power to make the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick person himself, according to what is necessary for treatment and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering occurs in many men in such a way that the paper above is stuck with egg white, and cannot move nor perform its natural tasks, then you must insert the point of a razor below the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps until you cut what is attached to the spatula's tip, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient can bear it if the spatula is too sharp or cuts the eye; and let your incision, from which you scrape off this assembly, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all of this assembly is healed, and sometimes they make in the eye salted water, and lift it with fresh water and collyrium; then place a linen bandage between the paper and the eye, and put wet wool moistened in egg yolk on top of the eye; and after the third day use collyrium and compresses until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles a hard, dry skin, and another which is not nervous but resembles moist, congealed skin, such that when touched with iron and tried to grasp with forceps, it cannot be done; both of these semblances begin towards the large tear gland and gradually increase until they cover all of the eye's vision and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient puts their head in your hand, then opens their eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then grasp the angle with small-forceps double, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put one horsehair or cow hair or ox hair on it, along with some strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the angle, and pierce through with the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and stretch it up, and scrape off all around the angle that surrounds the pupil and the sclera up to the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear gland using the spatula subtly and small-forceps, leaving the natural flesh of the tear gland so that by the incision tears do not flow in their accustomed manner; and sometimes stretch the angle with tweezers only, and thread, as we have said; then scrape it off entirely with a soft spatula.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the delicate tissue and break it, nor pierce the pupil; and after the incision sprinkle some crushed celandine into the eye, and use collyrium made of litargire, leaving it overnight; then cure with whatever is appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the angle is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle and tweezers cannot enter, this semblance of angle is often cured with medicines; and as I have described in the division, it appears that there are several kinds, and if you see one cut open, then open the eye of the patient and take a light spatula slightly bent in this manner:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently lift the angle upwards and if it does not seem to thin out and you see that the reason persists, then distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litargire and red collyrium and crushed celandine, and stop up the eye overnight; then recommence the other operation according to this same manner until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is any obstacle in the eye that prevents you from operating, such as a hot aposteme, then use milk first and cure the hot aposteme until it is healed; then recommence the operation as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the tear gland causes great harm to the eye, then suspend it with tweezers and cut off a part of it but not all, so that tears do not flow there; then distill red collyrium made of litargire into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	And about the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	**In the eyes of some men, there sometimes appears red flesh, which covers the pupil and presses on the papers around it, and resembles a cherry-red rose. The operation is such that the patient places his head in your hand, then you open his eyes, and coiled all this flesh with suitable tweezers for this purpose, and hold it firmly; then cut off the first flesh, and keep cutting right up to the end with the razor until finished, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation. The incision should be made with the scalpel that we have mentioned in the cutting of the nail and in small forces with which one removes the sebaceous matter, as the figure shows after this chapter. And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, then fill the eye with bruised wormwood or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines onto it, and place cotton dipped in egg white over the eye so that it may be securely covered from hot inflammation. And if anything remains, and hot blood mounts up to you, and you doubt about hot inflammation, then leave the eye and treat the inflammation with things that appease hot inflammation. Then return to your operation until it is healthy, and thus do for all the flesh that has adhered to the eye by this method.**
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it is necessary that you alleviate the cure of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the artificial way, in surgical operation with iron tools; and do not put your hand into any of these operations unless you see that these members are able to withstand this operation.
des voines des eulz	And about the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Before veins appear red which cover the eye, they obscure sight and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that you first examine if the eye, where veins appear, is swollen and if there is no other visible disease except for swelling; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to put their head on your knee, then suspend those veins along its course according to your skill, and let the suspension be delicate and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And hold two tweezers by degrees on one body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully squeeze those delicate veins,
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all this in one hour, then apply a plaster to the eye of things that alleviate the pain of the eyes, and let it stay for several days until the pain is alleviated and an abscess is formed, then resume according to this method which is stated beforehand until he is healed; and this is the form of the treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Physicians call a "fistula" an "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and with medicine that is hot and burning according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is treachery in it. You must cut open the abscess where it must burst, and draw out all the moisture that is inside until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption and blackness, then bring everything from the instruments that are present here according to this form; it is called "aspre chief" (sharp knife) and should be made of iron with a point like a chisel as shown in its current form
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then twist it between your fingers and press with your hand until you know that all the corruption has been removed. Do this several times, then return the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the area is solid and flesh does not appear, and the body of the bowels is solid, and remains so for 40 days, and it neither renews nor becomes an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healthy; but if not, then there is no other remedy than to redirect the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form: namely, uncover the bone a second time with iron and hot medicines, and when it has been uncovered, take a borer according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the borer be tapered to its tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the cheekbone, and move your hand away from the eye and pouch, then turn the drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it because the wind enters there if he holds his hand over his nose; and then restore to its place with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the joints, then the matter goes to the nose. Thus it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	About the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eye opens entirely and nothing disturbs it nor diminishes its size, then you must bind the patient. Then rinse the eye, then place cupping glasses or hot jars without burning to suck out matter, then put on the eye a linen made of aloe, acacia, incense, and sarcocolle, then strain the eye with bandages and cloths in this manner: take soft cloths, double each one four times, then place them on top of each other according to how much the eye needs; then strain it with a firm bandage from above, then restart the cupping glasses to suck without burning. Then remove the cups and leave the eye strained day and night. If the linen moistens too much, you must change it often. Then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see that the eye is improving, that's good; but if not, then restart the bandage and linen and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	About the bursting of an ocular vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption occurs in the ocular vein and opens up and paper comes out like a grain of resin, it is frightful to see. Then if you want to cover it, the procedure is as follows: take a needle and pierce it into the root of the part below until it reaches the part above, then take another needle with one doubled thread from the part by the eye socket; pierce this through and leave the first needle in place according to its position. Then sew up the site with the doubled thread and tie one part of the vein around it and strain it well, then remove the needle and place on the eye damp linen soaked in egg albumen. Leave it until the thread sticks with the vein, then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed. And sometimes the wound is restrained by the vein on each side with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye becomes greatly inflamed, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes out from the back of the eye and corrects the moisture of the albuginous humor and lets the eye descend, and enter into it quickly. Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	About the brow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bubble gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, yet it is not water. And the manner of its appearance when worked on is thus: have the patient sit on an appropriate and straight seat, then take his head between your two hands, and move it until you see the bubble rise to your eyes; then pierce it with a needle, and let it descend and disperse the light, and the patient sees things as he used to. And if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if its descent of the bubble is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	**If the patient sits between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make an incision through the conjunctive tissue with the cornea and the crown until the bow is released; and when it has been released, distill warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, into the eye, then treat it further until it is healed.**
des aigues de l’oil	Water of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	**We have here examples of waters used in dividing [the eye] and those which should be used for piercing; operate according to the health [of the patient].**
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	**You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight; cover the good eye and hold it tightly. Then place the paper for the eye in your left hand if the eye is on the left, or in your right hand if it is on the right. Next, take the instrument called 'almagda' in your right hand if the eye is on the left, or your left hand if it is on the right. Place the tip of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a ray from that corner of the eye towards the lesser lachrymal duct. Then insert the instrument called 'almagda' gently and twist your hand until you feel it reach the empty space in the corner of the eye. The measure of the path of almagda should be equal to the length from the width of a prune seed up to the end of the darkness; this is the crown of the eye. Then you will see the bone through the clear cornea, and then place the instrument where the water is and squeeze it along one pathway after another.**
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If water flows downwards now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a short time, if the water rises through the second pathway again, place the forceps with the instrument. Once it is inserted and it does not rise further, carefully extract the almagda by rotating your hand little by little; then put a little gem-silk into the water, and gently lift the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Next, place over the eye a plug of linen moistened in rose oil and egg yolk, and tie it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Nowadays, we put crushed cinnamon on top with plenty of egg yolks.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then pierce the conjunctiva alone, not too deeply but make it subtlely; then insert the almagda as we have said. When completed, prepare for the patient a suitable resting place where he sleeps on his back in a dark room; let him be deprived of all movements and eat light foods; do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition until the third day. Then untie him in the same dark house, examine his sight, and make him see some things before tying him again for seven days. Do not perform this during the operation or after incision immediately, but rather afterwards when water rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If a boil appears, then you should lance it on the sixth day, and use ointment that subdues inflammation; and when it is calmed, remove the bandage and put a plaster over it to cover it for some days, and keep it in this dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then let him leave the house little by little, and return to his usual activities; and know that no disciple should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Jericho, who told us that in some country they make almagda pierce the eye, from which they suck out the water, but nevertheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them, and they should be made of pure silver:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	"And their heads of these same subtlety are two, and one behind has three angles."
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nostrils
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various colored hairs are born, of which some seem like many-legged scorpions; and there are also such ones with hair enchanted in fox-colored hue, and soft hair of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of those hairs which are soft and not enchanted, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils and sprinkle the ointment on those hairs, and pull them strongly; then take what you can hold with the subtly sharp pointed tweezers on one side until you know that all the hair is gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	"And if there remains anything that cannot be cut off, then open it with one of the light and sharp instruments so that nothing remains. And if it swells or becomes inflamed, then treat it as is necessary; but if it is malignant swelling, then hurry and cauterize until the blood stops flowing, and all the flesh has been removed, then apply oil or vinegar to the bones."
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose bleeds and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healthy; but if moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is bone marrow in the bone above, which prevents the instrument from cutting. Therefore, you must insert a linen thread of moderate thickness, well soaked in hot water with spice between each knot at least one digit wide; and the patient should place the head of the thread in their nostril with some force and pull it out while smelling until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; children often do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wishes to do it. Then hold the head that comes out through the nose with one hand and the other head that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and guide them both gently in unison.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have rotted away the bone marrow. Then pull out the thread, wipe off the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back into the nose as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded all remaining bone marrow. Then insert a wick of lint into the nose for several days until it is healthy. If there is need for drying medicines, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	"And it should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a tube with its conduit likewise; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and the instrument full for purging the head; and let there be many holes at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid."
de la char sor le neis	To remove flesh from the nostrils
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	"Often there appears on the head of the nostril a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large so that it is visible to look at; therefore you must cut it off at the beginning and remove all of it, then put on it the cautery or the burning medicine. And if one waits too long to cut it until it has become large, take care if it is hard, of dark color, and poor sense; do not touch it with iron for it is an engrained swelling, because when it is cut, great mischief comes upon the patient. But if the swelling is soft to touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut off, then empty the nostril and cut it without fear, and cure it afterwards with drying and restrictive things."
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nostril is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuity occur in one of these cartilages, they profit little, whether in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this happens to anyone, then see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a stitch, then heal it until it is clean; but if the lips are already separated on both sides, then scrape all parts of their core until they are clean, then join the two lips with a stitch, tie them together, powder dragon's blood powder and crushed incense on top; put a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster on top, let it set by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is clean.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	"The manner of stitching is that you sew the wound together: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I have told you."
des apostemes des levres	Of the swellings on the lips
