A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men have within their lips hard abscesses, resembling grains of millet, small and large. Therefore, you must turn the lips, cut into each nodule, grasp it with forceps and cut it in every part; then apply powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stanched. Then apply the ointment of Aesculapius, and dress the area with dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times fleshy growths appear on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold them with forceps and cut at their root, allowing the vein or blood to run; then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the wound; if this flesh grows back after the incision, which happens often, then cut it again and cauterize it: it will not return after the cautery. These are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes escarps appear at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and sharp; sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish-green and worms come to the gum, causing foulness; therefore you must make the patient sit between your hands with their face in your lap and scrape away at the escarps until nothing remains; do the same for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains until they are all removed; if what caused them is removed first, that is good; otherwise restart on the second day and continue on the third until everything has been scraped off; know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping according to the task at hand, as those used to scrape between teeth differ from those used to scrape around them; have all these forms and others ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, it is necessary to wait before extracting until the pain has ceased, for one should never perform such an operation while the patient is in pain. For it is a delicate matter that requires great skill and offers no excuse for failure.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constricted by a draught, you must be certain of the throbbing tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient and they think it is in a wisdom tooth, and have the good tooth pulled out; but still the pain does not depart because the bad one remains, for we have seen this happen many times. And when you are certain of the throbbing tooth, then scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides; then move it with your thumbs or fine forceps little by little until it is well loosened, then firmly fix the forceps; and keep the patient's head steady between your legs so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take any of these tools and place it gently on each side, and with the lever move it as you have done previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and rotten, then you must fill it with wads where the holes are; and hold it gently with pliers so that it does not break while extracting; and much bleeding must be done around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And make sure you do not break it, and if a piece remains, it will return to the patient through the wickedness of the root causing even greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons who through their haste and recklessness sometimes break the jawbone, and bring about what we have mentioned here; but they often cause great illness through the infection of those remaining roots or the broken bone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the place with wine, vinegar, and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the place with crushed vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments used to extract teeth should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting a tooth. These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	"And let them be of heavy members so they do not bend at all during the pulling, and let them be of good iron well-made, and let them have teeth for holding moves."
de la racine des dens	"from the root of the teeth"
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	If the root remains at the draw, you must put moistened cotton smeared with butter for 1 or 2 days on the wound
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the joint is softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri", with which the head seems like a bird's beak; and shape them inside as if filing it.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali," that is, tweezers, this is the form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out, this is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, these forms come later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are placed on the surface of the teeth, and this instrument resembles large pliers, here is its form
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments should be strong enough not to break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted. And the wise master finds his instrument himself according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity. And if one breaks one's cart or other bones where it could be useful, then one searches among the instruments that are necessary, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, this is its form
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and hold well to hold the bone so that it does not escape but can grasp and remove it. Then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all this instrument
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to their natural shape, and their form is ugly, especially in young women, then you must know if the tooth is close behind the tooth and not in its proper place, and one cannot set it right or file it: then scrape it; and if it is against the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak and has iron pointed at the end
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And gently tap with your hand every day for the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent so that one can file it, then use a file like this whose form is like
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles. And gently file the tooth little by little every day so that it does not move too much until it falls out. Then smooth it at the end with any plane and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file off its sharpness until it is even enough not to cut the tongue nor corrupt speech
quant li dent lochent	When teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth before the opening falls out, either from blow or fall, and the patient cannot chew without the food escaping, even after treating it with constricting medicines, then you must constrain it with a gold thread.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the heads of the thread with a pair of pliers, and bring them together, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and hold it in place so that it does not injure the tongue; then let it remain thus tightly as long as it can endure, and if it loosens or the threads break, then bind it with another thread; thus it will remain and serve throughout its duration, and this is the shape of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy ones, and of the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it should be replaced in its place little by little as we have said. And only those who are wise and skilled should undertake this task, and sometimes they make the shape of a tooth from cow bone and put it in the place where there is a gap and tighten it with wire as we have described, and it will remain in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this tie comes under the tongue or naturally; or by accident of a healed wound; and its operation is as follows: you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your lap, and lift their tongue up. Then grasp the nerve-like tie with broad forceps until the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is any hardness or knot, which comes from the healing of a wound, then insert the nail-scraper and cut through it with broad forceps; but be careful that the incision is not too deep, because the artery lies underneath. And when you have done this, then apply a compress of rose water and sage, or cold water, and place a linen pad under the tongue each night so that the head does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is a flow of blood, place powdered vitriol on the wound. And if the blood continues to flow, cauterize it with a slow-acting cautery that is good for this purpose. Then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of dusky color or black or hard, but the patient does not feel it, do not touch it because it is a chancre. And if it tends to become an ulcer and there is moisture present, then use a needle and make a small incision with a sharp scalpel and remove it from both sides. If bleeding occurs during your procedure, sprinkle powdered vitriol until it stops bleeding. Then continue your procedure until all the flesh is removed. Then rinse the area with sage and honey and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes in the throat there appear growths called 'godath', which are properly called tonsils. If you treat them as we have said earlier, but they do not heal, then beware: if they are hard tumors with a small opening and dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of bleeding. But let it ripen until it becomes soft, and then you can remove it, or it will burst on its own. And if it is white and has a small root, prepare the instrument to cut it out, but first check if the abscess is warm, rests quietly, and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then seat the patient before the sun, and let their head rest in your hand. Have them open their mouth and take the serum between your hands, pressing the tongue from below with all instruments, of which this is the form; and it should be made of fine silver or brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against all this instrument? And when you see the boil, take the lancet and insert it into the head of it, and twist it up above as much as you can; then draw out some of the cloth with it, and cut off the instrument, of which here is the shape, resembling a crow's foot; and its ends are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use pincers, of which here is the shape
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and pointed on the other; and when you have cut off one of the kernels, then cut off the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle with hot water and salt-water, and if there is any bleeding, gargle with water in which pomegranate skins have been cooked, or myrtle leaves, or similar things, until the blood is stanched; then treat it until it is healed. And sometimes other boils appear in the throat besides the two kernels, so cut them off likewise as you would the two kernels.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was near the throat, specifically one that was small in size. The swelling had closed almost all of her throat so that she could not exhale through the obstructed passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if left untreated for two days
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was already so swollen that it had pushed out both ears through the nostrils
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly proceeded to insert a needle into one nostril and draw out much pus; afterwards I inserted another needle into the other nostril and opened her mouth, pressing down on her tongue. Then I inserted the needle into the abscess and cut away part of it, releasing only a little blood. Thus the woman's throat passage was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine. But I kept cutting away at the abscess for a long time, and it continued to grow back, filling up the space that I had emptied until it became very large again. Then I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing. And I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	The eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it rises up to the eyelid, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; but if it is below and thick and round, it is called "uve.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, but you see that the surrounding swelling has subsided, and it appears thin, then you must cut it open; and if it is round and well-formed and not long, and it is sanguineous or reddish-black in color, then you must avoid incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient thereby.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to its appearance and length, make the patient sit before the sun, press their tongue with the instrument mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eyelid and pull it underneath, cutting with the two instruments I have mentioned in the incision of two lymph nodes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond its natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves both voice and speech. And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two amygdalae, until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears being cut, you must use a device for cauterizing that fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient places their head in your hand, and then you press the tongue with the instrument mentioned in the cautery chapter, and apply hot water with a little salt so that it is not too thick or too clear; and using this instrument carefully, here is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has at the top a small vessel where one puts the medication, like the horn of a spoon, and puts the instrument with all the medicine on the eyelid; and the patient should lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth away from the medicine and the eyelid, so that it does not reach the throat and cause swelling. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eyelid for about half an hour until you see that it is darkened and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above until the cotton touches the eyelid; do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after 4 or 5 days. And if you need to start the cauterization again with the medicine, then restart it, and afterwards wipe around the eyelid with cotton soaked in oil, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water and gargle until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more gentle than cutting or cauterization. If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and chamomile and similar herbs, and mix them all together or some of them into one pot; put a little incense inside, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with earthenware, and there should be one small vessel like this inside the pot:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is made of silver or bronze, and one of its heads is inserted into the patient's mouth until steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye is cauterized. Afterwards repeat often until the eye dries up, but make sure not to do this at the beginning of an inflamed abscess, as many things can happen there; and do not do it too far beyond the decline of heat.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put an egg shell on its end so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the egg shell does not let the vapor hurt the mouth, and this together with health is good care.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, a bone or fish spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; therefore you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue with the instrument so that you can see it move; and whatever is not visible and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of flaxseed, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches its place, it will be visible, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take one instrument made of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at its end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have its end raised up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest the whole thing go down, nor push the bone in too far; and it is better for the patient themselves to insert the instrument, for they will know where the thing has lodged itself; then draw it out gently along the entire length of the instrument until it comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	de la sansue de la gorge
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Blood is sometimes treated, as I have said in the division, by medicinal treatment. But if this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, and then press the tongue with the instrument I mentioned.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, then treat it with a small iron pin or with fine forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a headed cane and put it into the throat of the patient, and then put red-hot iron on the head of the cane, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take plenty of cold water and open the mouth, pour it in without letting it be swallowed, and move it with your hand frequently. And as soon as the blood feels the water, it will stop flowing.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without troubling.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The manner of the fumigation is that you take one pot which has live coals in it, and its mouth is covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and into this hole place the head of the instrument. Then throw your fumigation onto the coals, and the patient places the end of the tube in their mouth and closes their lips so that no smoke escapes, but reaches the eye. And the stone will now fall out, and if it does not, then recommence the fumigation many times; and let the patient thirst, and eat salty and bitter foods, and do not drink water. And then it will be necessary for the stone to pass by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood clot is this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved tongs for entering into the throat; and it has the shape of a crow's beak, and has sharpness like a file, so that whatever it takes hold of, it cannot let go. And here you see its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings forth here from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two manners among them, one being like its own kind, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those places where abscesses are located on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the bowels have died according to their fullness; and there are some that must be pierced when they are ripe, even if they do not die on their own.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and they are left until they have rotted around, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay perforating it until it is dead, it will harm the main limb. But where it is near the fundament, pierce it before it dies. It is not necessary to pierce a hard abscess without digestion completed, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it rot deeply and become elongated inside, and a fistula occur; and it cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the hour for piercing an abscess that has died according to its course, and this is when the pain has ceased, and the division of the fever, and the decrease of the pain and redness, and from bursting and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the piercing lower down where the abscess depends more, and where it opens most; and let the piercing be long like the body of a finger, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints near nerves and arteries, and in all smooth places where there is no wrinkle."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those cases where they affect, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy location, it is better that you delay perforating until it is confirmed with digestion completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	But if you pierce it before that time, the body of the venom will be elongated, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depth of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses should be pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring small incisions for small abscesses, small openings; and for large abscesses, large openings, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; And there are such abscesses where it is necessary to insert hot coals, and cover them when they have become like embers and softened, then you must do likewise as one does with blisters: And there are those that are cut into three angles, and there are those from which one cuts like the leaf of a mulberry tree, such as angelic abscesses; And there are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as soft superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly; And when the abscess is large and has drawn much bowels, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the bowels at once, but draw out a part; Then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again afterwards; Do this many times little by little, until all the bowels come out; Likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying child, or young infants, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes jumps at the release of the bowstring, which by chance causes the death of the patient, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore study this chapter carefully, and when you have pierced your abscess, open the wound and examine if the wound from the abscess is small. And if it is a full incision, then bring linen or old cotton pads; and if it is a large abscess with many holes, then you must insert one pad into each so that they come together. And if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and scraped around it, then you must fill it with dry cotton or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if flows of blood occur during your procedure, then bring cold water and towels, wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply governance and care, and the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book, especially in wintertime when the location of the abscess is very nervous. In such case, you should place moistened cloths and bandages in hot wine and oil upon it; but if it's in summertime and the spot is fleshy, then you must apply damp cloths in cold water and oil, or in wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said. Then remove the bandage, cleanse and treat it until it's healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this one must know universally in the cure of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the cure of abscesses, and here is that chapter."
des soros	Here are some translations of the word "soros" from Middle French to English:
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head meets the neck come small abscesses, resembling those of chickens in their skin, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fleshy and moist like chickens; but there are also those that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt that they block the arteries.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you should test all instruments called 'entromissoire', from which the form comes later, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	But if it contains moisture, then close it with a long stitch.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape clean without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, because it returns again if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will chase away what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then recommence with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and on the third, until you know well that there is no longer anything left of the night; then dress the wound with suitable ointment, until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds much fat, cut it according to this form with a long incision; and sprinkle your onions on it, scrape it from all sides, and pay great attention to drawing out the coat where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I tell you later.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do for an abscess if it is hard, and with cutting and dressing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting of a hard and moist abscess is easier, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And some of these abscesses have no moisture at the head, and there are those hard abscesses that I cut from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, which could not be broken; and if one had struck it with anything, it would have made a wound like that of a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come at the head, especially those which come at the heads of children and at the roots of ears, always open them at the lowest point to allow the bowels to escape; and dress them as is necessary.
des scrophules	scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin; sometimes they also come elsewhere on the body, and there are many of them, and they intertwine with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each boil is properly within its own hide, such as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many kinds similar to these boils.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others malignant that refuse to yield to healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, if you see one that is well-disposed to touch and resembles the color of flesh, moves freely on each side and is not hard by the nerves of the neck or artery or vein, nor deep; then you should cut it open from above, scrape off its surface on all sides, and keep the lips of the wound closed with compresses if necessary, as we have said regarding head abscesses. And remove it bit by bit, ensuring that you do not cut into the nerve or vein, nor use a sharp or cutting knife, lest your hand slip and cut deeper than intended.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and blood does not allow you to work, then place powdered vitriol or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and hold the wound tightly; keep it like this until the abscess is soothed, and the wound begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding stops, return to your work until you finish it; then check on your fingers for any small scabs, if there are any cut and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, then it is not necessary to cut that scab at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off naturally; then fill the wound with cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scab, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up tightly; for there will be no excess left due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you must understand to cover the root of it, and draw fire, and the cut as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold excessiveness, prick where it appears dead; and prick thus as the one before said, depending, then bring tent with ointment and similar things, so it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then cure with ointment entering flesh until it is sound.
de squinance	de squinance
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the operation of cutting a throat, but I never saw it done in our land, and that is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have quinsy, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and one does not receive help through this, for all the veins and the vessels of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the vessels, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three circles or four with a small slit across between two circles or according to the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long inside.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat all around the hinge, then cut into the heart until it reaches the chin; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cover the syfac as we have said; and it is proven by the section of the nerve of the chin that spouts fire where it is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour of doubt about strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked off, and the patient is judged to be near death, and his breathing has failed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, thus guarding against death; and for this reason, the ancients ordered that the wound should remain open until the worst of the illness has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they commanded that the wound be sutured and dressed until it was healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting some of the channels of the lungs; and I was called to treat her, but found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that the blood issuing from it was not from the veins or arteries but only from the throat, and the breath was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sutured the wound, treating it until it was healed; and the young lady suffered nothing but hoarseness of voice, returning afterward to her usual condition. Therefore I say that cutting the epiglottis should not be feared.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large one with the color of a fig, and it often occurs in women. It has two types: natural and accidental; however, the natural type does not have any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type has two forms: one is similar to fatty tissue, while the other resembles an abscess that comes from an artery. One should be cautious and only operate with fire for those that are small, and first test and search through the entire passageway: if you find it like the aforementioned fatty tissue, and not connected to any vein, cut it as one cuts fat, removing all of it until there is none left; then carefully examine everything and treat it accordingly so that it becomes perfectly healthy.
des nous	of fatty tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many types of fatty tissue, all of which I will describe; however, now I must discuss the difference between fat and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	"I say that an abscess is hot and feverish until the suppuration has passed, at which point it becomes filled with pus, and then the fever and heat subside."
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the knot, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains syrupfac, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a jar, and becomes large; and they are either fatty or moist, and most of them have the color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	"When treating a fatty tumor, it is necessary to first examine and express the contents using an instrument called the 'intromittor', according to the shape described in the following chapter."
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The manner of inquiring into the apostemes of the nose is that you take the moistest part that you find in the aposteme, and twist your two fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the aposteme; then extract the intruder, and beware of what jumps out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture is thin, whatever its color may be, open it as I said for other apostemes; and if no moisture comes out after the instrument, know that it is fatty, then cut it in a cross shape, grasp it with tweezers, lightly scrape each side, and watch the skin where it lies, pull it out whole with the knot; and if you cannot pull it out whole, pull it out in pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If anything remains there, the wound will reopen many times; and if a little remains and the blood grievously festers, then apply to the wound some corrosive waters and powders, bind the wound, and place soothing substances for an inflamed abscess, continuing other treatments until it is healed; and if the wound is large, cut away the two lips of the wound, treating those that encroach upon flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if a vein is beating nearby or another complication arises, quickly apply powdered vitriol to the area, leaving it on for two or three days until the wound becomes suppurated and the inflammation of the blood subsides, then return to remove any remaining fatty tumor."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the instruments for dilating fistulas, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small. There are four square ones called "albarets" and one called "breb." They also come in three sizes to encircle fistular abscesses, similar to those used for sewing curses. They are made of citrine brass, iron, or silver. Those made of yellow brass are the best, but blackened ones are more commonly used to encircle the openings of fistulas. They come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the onions are in many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are also onions with two curves of three kinds; and there are those with three curves, which are also of three kinds; and there are those with two curves, and onions with only one curve, which are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these are cutting, and there are some that do not cut but only on one side, with which one scrapes the nails to avoid cutting the vein or nerve; and among these instruments are the alembic spoons used in many hands so that the patient does not notice them when opening abscesses; and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only on thick flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument resembling a pair of tweezers according to this shape, with which one stops blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the location where veins and arteries are severed or where there has been excessive bleeding. Sometimes they are made in this larger size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupted, appearing like those of a woman; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to treat them must follow this form as far as line .b. up to .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape away the fat and dress the wound with healing herbs. Then bring together the two lips of the wound to stitch them closed, and continue treating it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size as happens in women, then make two similar incisions above, one touching the other at their ends so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape away the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever else is necessary in treatment until it is healed; and if it does not heal, or if the incision was not complete because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment. Leave it there until it eats away the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	"Abscesses of the armpits"
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"The abscesses that occur under the arms are usually hard tumors resembling scrofula or have rough surfaces, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the boil has been drained out, then fill the wound with soft cotton, and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and dress it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the boil resembles scrofula, then cut it as we have said for scrofula wounds, and if the wound fills with pus again, then apply a cauterization as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is severed and the skin above it is closed, many abscesses often form, and likewise happens when a vein bursts open; and one can thus recognize this when the abscess is long and deep. When you feel it with your fingers, you sense pulling; but when it's due to a vein, then disfigurement appears clearly. It is foolish to cut into such an abscess, especially if it's under the buttocks or armpits, around the neck, and in many other locations, where it becomes very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid cauterization and cutting into the wound. Instead, if it's an arterial swelling that has pierced the skin deeply, first cut through the fat around the arteries and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it's exposed. Then insert a needle underneath one side of the artery and push it through to the other side, tying the artery with a double thread in two places as I have shown you for extracting two temporal arteries. Next, prick the point between the two ligatures with an introjector until all the blood comes out, then drain the abscess and clean it well. Then apply dressings so that they stick to the wound, using appropriate ointments until it's healed. If the swelling is due to a vein incision, then you should take a needle in your hand from where the swelling begins to its end on the skin, insert it underneath the point you're holding with your hand and push it through, tying a double thread so that you can pull it out from the other side. Then tie the abscess as I have told you, using two heads of thread tied together in two places. If you doubt whether the threads are secure, then insert another needle along the entire length of the thread underneath the first incision and tie them off at four points. Then cut into the abscess until all the superfluities come out, then cut away the excess skin around the heart and leave what's tied. Finally, apply a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, and apply dressings with ointments until it's healed.
des apostemes des ners	of boils on the nerves
