Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, just as boils come to the artery and vein, so too do boils appear on the nerves when they are injured or from excessive exertion, etc.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often in shoulders and hips and in all places where there are joints, and it is the worst kind of abscesses, with a color similar to that of the body. It is present in many different conditions without pain; however, when pressed strongly, the patient feels pain not deep in the body but beneath the heart. It moves well in all directions but does not go forward or backward nor up nor down. One should not attempt to cover it with iron as this might cause contraction. Those that are on the head or forehead are painful at the temples.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, grasp it with tweezers and cut it at its root; if it is large, suspend it with forceps and scrape it off, then remove the skin and sew the wound closed until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of hanging warts
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes this happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is an illness called 'fungus' due to its resemblance to one. The roots are thin and the heads large; some are small and others very large. I saw a man who had two on his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, with no difference between them. They were white, had fine roots, and were often split open, with moisture constantly flowing from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found that one was XVIII ounces in weight and the other VI З. The operation of the incision is such that you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is pale and moist with a subtle root; then cut it with a broad spatumile, and have the cautery on fire ready.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	When cutting, there are often too many large flows of blood. If your hand slips, quickly apply the cautery. And if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made linen thread, tie it around the artelul as we have described, and leave it for two days; then restrict it, and keep pulling on the linen thread until it cuts through the artelul, removing it without difficulty. And if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting even the belly, but you can cut half of it, cauterize it so that it does not return, then dress the wound, and be careful not to cut the thelul which has a rust color, poor sense, and produces milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	"For this is an incurable tumor, and I will discuss the treatment for cancer later on."
quant li boude ist fuer	"When the wound has healed"
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cauterization of a wound or a fissure of the scrotum, and is on the belly and in some cases on the buttocks, as it happens in other hernias, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what precedes, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rupture of the scrotum and the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the boil resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and has various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the bursting of the intestine, then it becomes more diverse; and when it is pressed with two fingers it sinks in and then returns, and sometimes it is hard, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the anus during difficult labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, not constraining at all; and if it is due to blood, then the boil appears large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and its appearance shows whether it is from arterial blood, venous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary for you to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Because there is doubt and fear about it, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If the appearance is for the intestine or the belly button, then you should command the patient to lie on their back, with their arms extended straight out, and have them turn onto one side. Then place the patient lying flat between your hands, and proceed around the area you have marked with all the instruments. Then extend half of the abscess above the ligature with all the large forceps; then tie it tightly around with a strong string or cord made of fine silk thread, leaving the knot untied. Then open half of the abscess extended over the ligature and insert your index finger inside to find the intestine. If you find that it is caught in the ligature, release it and bring the intestine out from the front of the abdomen. And if you find the belly button, then cut away any excess tissue; if the artery or vein opposes you, carefully go around it again, return to your work and take two needles and attach them to two strong threads. Insert the two needles crosswise into where you pierced earlier; then hold the abscess at three points above the needles with forceps, and if it opens, remove the needles and leave the area until it can suppurate naturally and cut away any dead tissue there. Then cure the area according to what is needed, and cauterize the abscess as we have said; then extract any blood or moisture you find, then cure the area as required and suture the wound closed.
dou chancre	Of a chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the section on the signs of a chancre and how one should treat it with medicines, and how to avoid surgical treatment. Now we will discuss a chancre that is spreading to the marrow and requires great caution in its treatment. The ancients said that when a chancre appears where it can be scraped off like those found on the breast or hip, then all of it must be removed at the beginning; but if it is large and old, one should not approach it because I have never seen anyone heal from one, nor have I heard of any such case before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operation is performed where it can be removed, as we have said, it is done thus: first purge the patient with black colic; then make them vomit if they show signs of repletion, and prepare the patient a good place to perform the operation. Then grasp the chancre with tweezers and cut it all around and remove it completely without leaving anything behind. Let the blood flow freely and squeeze the wound with your hand or some other object until bleeding stops. If bleeding from the incision of an artery or vein hinders you, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have previously discussed the similarities of dropsy in our division, and how the gathering of water is formed, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only 'eclites' is mentioned; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: namely tympanites and hippocratic coughs, for they are deadly things; therefore when you treat this dropsy similarity called 'eclites' with medicine, and the cure does not help, look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as indigestion and similar things. Do not touch them with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient to be strong and vigorous, and they do not have any other illness but dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lift the patient upright onto your hands, and the assistants press the belly outwards pushing the water towards the lowest part of the chest, then take the spatula spinous in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Pierce it with a point, but do not pierce too deeply lest it reach the intestines when inserted, and do not let it bleed. Then see if dropsy has entered near the intestines: you must make an incision three fingers' breadth directly below the navel; if dropsy is due to liver disease, the incision should be made on the left side of the third fingerbreadth; if it is due to worms, it should be made on the right. Ensure that the patient does not lie on the incision so that superfluities do not flow into this weak area. Then pierce all the skin with the instrument and insert it, raising your hand between the skin and the sinew as in flaying, to the breadth of one nail or about there; then pierce the sinew until the spatula reaches the empty space, which is the location of the water; then draw forth the instrument, and insert this one instead. Here is its form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is like a thin silver rod, and it is made of gold or light arrowhead material, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one more; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that writers use to cut feathers:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it then descends onto the instrument; empty out either half or a third of it now, for if you empty more than is necessary at this time, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's power signify, and his pulses; then draw out the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the heart that stops up the hole that is on the face, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then recommence the instrument the following day, if you see the patient enduring these things, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this for a few days, and guard against leaving too much but only a little drop of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient, and leave much water on him, so treat it with hot burial or hot sand, and by much sweat or bath and sun, and dye for drinking; and treat it with drying medicines until it is dry, and cauterize it on the stomach and liver and spleen after removing the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	The section on impotence is titled "De l'estopement de la verge" which means "On the stoppage of the penis". This refers to erectile dysfunction or impotence. The text discusses the causes and treatments for this condition.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or with a small one, or one that is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it must be pierced promptly with a very fine needle according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put the thin plug of lead in the hole and tie it tight and hold it thus for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps there will be no need for it, because urine that comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose hole is small shall use lead plaster, as we have said, so it may widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is not in its proper place are hindered. For some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis upward; and they cannot ejaculate because semen cannot reach the marrow, and this is a severe illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	The technique for performing a circumcision is as follows: have the patient lie on their back. Then grasp the glans of the penis and cut it around like the tip of a feather quill so that the urethral opening remains in its proper position. Be careful not to cause bleeding, which can occur frequently during this procedure. If bleeding does occur, use something that stops bleeding and treat any resulting wound until it has healed.
des pustules de la verge	Of the blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these blisters appear on the penis, and there is an ugly appearance of skin; and some are malignant and others benign. Therefore you must take them with tweezers, squeeze them out and clean all of them thoroughly, then put wet cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then apply the ointment diaphoretic until it is gone.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the navel is inflamed, of foul color and smelling bad, you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it off, and if the navel is high on the penis, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the piece that is inside. And when it is healed, then treat the outside part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if you treat both parts together, the head of the penis may not be securely closed, and blackness and corruption will come to its interior and the coition. So you must cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from honey and flour mixed with ground pomegranate rind and figs, and then treat it further until it is healthy again.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And the cauteries help in two conditions combined: namely, for bleeding and corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you should place a tube of lead into the opening of the penis, so that the patient can urinate through it. And when the skin at the tip of the penis becomes attached, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or occurs due to wound or abscess, then you must burn it with the hair-removing instrument until the adhesions are severed and the head of the penis is freed from all sides. And if it is difficult to separate them, then you should burn a little at the tip of the penis and skin with the spatula. Then gently separate them, and place a thin, moistened linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, so that they do not adhere again.
de la circoncision	Et se c’est un garcon qui doit estre circoncis, si covient que tu coupes le pelz a .vi. mois, et les autres enfans a .xii. mois; et il est bon quant tu les feras circonsire quant l’enfant aura .iii. ans ou environ.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in its continuity; nevertheless, when we perform this operation willingly and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work with the least harm possible.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children because it was not part of their law, and we only have knowledge of it through experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the majority of masters and surgeons who perform circumcision around one dal, and by force, and for an entire novacule; so it was that the heart would flee because there are two tissues, and sometimes one cuts the upper one and leaves the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Otherwise they cover it up and the pain is doubled, and at the time of cleansing the point of the member is not secure; and sometimes during cleansing of the foreskin the knife slips and ruins the operation, and many times it happens that they do not need cleansing, which I have seen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Regarding the cleansing done by force, I have found that using a thread tied around the entire length is the best experiment because the force cuts equally well both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand thus, cut evenly throughout the whole tension; but let the thread be tightly wrapped around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he hears, that you are only tying the thread around the rod, and then let him enjoy all the ways you can; then hold him upright between your hands, and press down with your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them nor any tools; then place your hand on the rod and blow toward the heart, and pull it up until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place shut with a double thread, then tie it under one knot to another; and hold it with both hands by the second knot near the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two knots, then quickly lift up the heart and pull out the head of the rod; then let the blood flow freely from one opening to another, for this is the mother's womb; and sprinkle powder on top, and on the powder place a gauze bandage made from a cooked egg yolk tempered with rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, then treat further as needed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	"The form of the instruments for cleansing should be as follows: the two tips should be thin and sharp, and the tips should also be as large as a hazelnut, equal in size:"
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	"The error of cleansing occurs when the heart is inside the incision, therefore it is necessary to extend it with your fingernail before the wound becomes inflamed; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then use forceps, and then cut it."
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	"And if it lasts for three days and the part below the staff is swollen, let it be until the inflammation has subsided, then gently scrape off the scab; cut as much as you can move without harming the part of the staff, for it will not harm it."
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Therefore treat the wound with quick-acting powder, as we have said when treating powders, and if you cut too much from the heart and it goes upwards, it will not harm. Treat it therefore as we have said until it heals."
dou retenement de l’urine	"On the retention of urine"
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by the blockage of a stone, or congealed blood, or bowels, or flesh newly born, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if urine is not released, and you see that there is a blockage due to a stone located at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to bend over on their knees; and place their feet on the ground behind them, and stretch out their belly towards the back, and have the patient lean forward as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder will be forced open from above to release the stone, so that urine flows out; and if it does not come out, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction using all the instruments called "syringe", the form of which is: and let it be made of thin, light silver, like a bird's feather; and let the tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be thin at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	To draw out urine, take a doubled thread and tie it to the top of a wad of wool or cotton. Insert the thread's end into the syringe. Cut off any excess wool and insert it up to the syringe's top. Then oil the syringe with olive oil and melted wax. Have the patient sit on a chair. Oil their bladder and penis with warm olive oil, molten wax, and cold water. Lightly place the syringe in the penis until it reaches the root. Then fold the penis upwards towards the belly. Insert the syringe further until the patient feels it reach the bladder. If not done correctly due to a bent tube, pull out the thread slowly, following the wool wad. Urine will follow the wool. Remove the syringe and allow urine to flow. Repeat the process until the bladder is empty and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	"On the diseases of the bladder"
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	"When there is erosion or blood in the bladder, or putrefaction has accumulated there, and you see that watery and medicinal substances are being discharged, then use all the instruments called a 'clepsydra', of which this is the form:"
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the raised area by which the medical cautery should be placed so that it stops up the tube well without additional pressure, so that moisture can be drawn out, and inserted when needed; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, place the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw what is inside; then draw the moisture into the catheter, and then strongly push the catheter back in; thus the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema used to enemize the bladder.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher up; and below there is one opening where the string falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put inside it the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie it between two breasts firmly with a doubled thread, and heat this moisture on the fire until boiling point; then place the tip of the catheter in the tube, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has passed into it, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, make a circle out of it, pierce it roundly around the edge; then strongly insert the thread into these holes, then join the circle together like closing a door, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it onto the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"on stones"
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	"I have already discussed in the section on stones their different types and methods of extraction along with medicinal remedies. I also explained the difference between stones that enter through the rains and all the signs associated with them, as well as which stones require surgical intervention - both in the bladder and in the penis. I will now explain this briefly and clearly."
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	"I say that stones which enter the bladder occur most frequently in children. This is a sign that urine is being expelled from the bladder like water in its fineness. The child will strain and grind his penis and frequently urinate until it becomes painful. In many cases, this condition is accompanied by inflammation. Children under the age of four usually have an easy recovery, while older adults find it much more difficult. Those who are middle-aged fare moderately well. The cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones."
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	When we come to treat, first cleanse the patient with an enema to draw out all the feces in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders finding the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and raise and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out near the top. Then have him sit between your hands and put his hands under his thighs so that the bladder is completely tilted downward. Then search for it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in its place, quickly cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall out upon touching the whole, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is an adult. Then insert it into his anus and search for the stone; when you feel it on your finger, press it against the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger and push the stone out where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands that with his right hand he stretch the scrotum upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the scrotum in the part where the incision is made; then insert the spatula like this, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between those who are between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight over the stone, and your two hands always on the fundament, and let the cut of the traverse be so that it is wide at its mouth and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the hand that is on the fundament causes it to fly forth without labor. And know that there are such stones with angles and edges: they are difficult to extract. And there are those that are beneath, resembling a gland, round, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those stones with angles and edges, make the cut larger. If it does not pass, then you must extract using tongs that are like a file at the head, to grab the stone so that it does not escape; or you place beneath it a subtle curved instrument at the end. And if you cannot grasp it thus, then enlarge the hole around the passage. If blood spurts forth, then stop it with vitriol. If there are more than one stone, first place the largest in the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then draw it out, and afterward extract the smaller ones if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be opened wider and a larger incision made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then two things happen to the patient: either they die or urine begins to flow constantly through the opening that cannot be closed. Nevertheless, make every effort to extract it with forceps, cutting it into pieces until you have completed your work. Then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, bind it, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine or oil and rose water and cold water on top to cool the hot abscess. Then have the patient rest on their back, and do not untie the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove the bandage, wash the wound area very well with oil and water, then apply ointment of diacereion and ointment of basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corrosions appear in the wound, and congealed blood forms in the bladder, causing urine to be retained in such a way that it flows out suddenly with urine: then cauterize the wound, remove that blood because if any remains, it will corrupt the bladder. Then wash the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and assist the patient in all ways you know until they are healed. And every time you treat them, tie their two thighs together and apply the medications to the affected area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passageway of the penis, stuck inside, and urine cannot flow out; then the treatment I mentioned earlier applies: cut there many times until relieved by this cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron needle according to this shape and with three points stuck into a splinter of wood
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move backwards into the bladder; then insert the probe gently into the penis until it reaches the stone; then turn the probe in your hand against the stone, little by little, until you can pierce the stone on the other side; then urine will come quickly, and then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is still inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks quickly and comes out with the urine, then the patient is healed. And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the penis at the location of the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, untie the thread, cleanse the wound from the blood clots, and treat it until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	de la piere des femmes
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone enters into women's urethra, and if it does happen sometimes, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: firstly, because by chance the woman may be a virgin; secondly, because one cannot find a woman who is well-informed and willing to uncover herself before physicians
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	**And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more hidden than the stone of the man, therefore a deeper cut must be made, and there is great fear involved. And if you should lack such [a person], then it is necessary that you take a midwife well-versed, and hardly ever will one find her, and if you do not find her, then seek any skilled mid-wife; and present to her a wise woman knowledgeable in the lives of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her that she perform whatever you command concerning the examination of the stone; and observe very carefully if the woman is virgin: then it is necessary for her to place her thumb upon the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, let her press it down with her thumb, and recommend that she place her thumb into the vagina of the patient, and press and move her left hand strongly upon the bladder.**
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder downwards until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the penis, where it appears moved apart, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the cut be initially small; then insert the probe into the cut if you feel the stone so close to the wound that the stone can come out fiery, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	and know their similarities for knowing the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood becomes faint, then place crushed vitriol on the wound and let it stay there for an hour until the blood is staunched; then return to your work until the stone comes out fiery, and have tools that I have told you about in extracting stones from men to help you in your work. And if the blood becomes faint because of the artery being cut, place powder on the wound and compress it with bandages and linen cloths, do not recommence this again, and leave the stone alone without trying to remove it because perhaps the patient might die; then dress the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has been stopped, and the place is ready, then return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	Here is the translation of the given text with a focus on the term "hernie carnosous":
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquatic hernia is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white seed, which is under the skin of the thighs containing the egg; and it is called "seed," and sometimes properly in the fabric of the egg, so that one might think there is another egg; and this happens if not punctured.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia comes from weakness that affects the thighs, and this matter becomes spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it occurs from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either declining towards jaundice, or colorless, black, or watery white; these are signs to recognize this condition, for if it is sac-like as we have said, then the abscess is ready, about the length of an egg figure, and does not open the joints, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is ready with part of an egg, and thus it seems like another egg; but if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the sac-like area, one can feel it well. Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, use a square-shaped probe, the shape of which is shown above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	"Therefore, according to what comes after the introite, judge what is inside."
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we open it with an iron tool, the patient must be seated according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then let him lie on his back, supported on something slightly raised, and place many cloths beneath him. Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the probe towards one of the two ribs near the joints. Then take the spatula lightly and cut the skin of the joints among the long line near where the knife points, making the cut straight down to the sac-like white area, and scrape it subtly according to your ability. Then pierce the sac full of water with a wide hole, and drain all the water, then place your bandages, stretching the sac upwards; and do not touch the rib cage itself, but only the sac. Cut away all or in pieces the surrounding skin subtly, so that if you do not cut it cleanly, the water will return. And if the egg slips out of your work, put it back in its place once you have completed the work on the sac. Then sew up the two layers of the rib cage with a stitch, then heal it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, then tie up the vessels that are suspended there, stopping the flow of blood. Then cut open the lung at all the suspensory ligaments and remove the egg, treating it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if water is gathered in two parts together, know that these are the roots; then cut the other part evenly as you did the first, then squeeze out the blood, and place clean linen moistened with rose oil on the wound. Then place another linen moistened in wine and oil over both wounds, and cover it with doubled cloth, and tie it all according to this manner:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips of cloth, and fill them with wool lint according to this manner, and sew them together at the waistband of the breeches. Let one end rest on the buttocks up to the back, and the other at the elbow area; then tie both ends over the two angles, and let all the bandage be gathered in the loop of the breeches. And sometimes this root is medicated by cautery instead of iron cutting, so take a fine cautery scalpel, cut through the skin at the roots, and heat it as we have said, until the white membrane that contains the water is exposed. Then take the cautery in this manner, prick through that membrane once, and burn off this subtle cautery.

Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	**And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to undergo this procedure due to its unpleasantness, perform perforation as I instruct you; for when you are certain by the signs that we have said that there is putrid matter inside, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at its lower part with a broad spatula and insert the trocar into the body's length; and make the hole wide so all the pus can flow freely; then place cotton on the site and tie it, leaving some space for the remaining pus to flow out, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the bandage does not allow the pus to exit through the mouth of the wound, you must insert a feather or the instrument used to treat dropsy, whose form is shown before; and widen the wound's opening, knowing that the pus will return and gather after six months or so, and when it has gathered as before, thus the patient will pass their days.**
de l’aposteme des coions	"On boil on buttocks"
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in cutting this vein there is danger and more often harmful conditions, therefore it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the operation and its like of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	"I say therefore that many boils come on the body, especially on the buttocks; and this happens often."
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known through sour and sharp acidity that spreads to the joints or percussion points; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; it does not cause pain, yet it is a severe abscess; sometimes one finds abscesses that are pale and thin-skinned with a reddish hue, and occasionally they arise from an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the hot appearance of the abscess when pressed with two fingers; and one must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is made from a vein swelling is known by its appearance upon touching with two fingers, and one can easily perform an incision on this type of boil as well as others; firstly cut around the joints, then raise the edge upwards, and carefully remove the white core from around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hard with these new feathers, then you must draw out the egg and cut its head; and if it is air in the syrinx or in those that are inside the vessels, then you must release all of this tension and roundly cut the head.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	"And if the birthmark of the skin is in the hinder part, then it is necessary that you cut off all of it and remove the boil as we have said."
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when your procedure is completed, then fill the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it is healed."
de l’aposteme des coions	"On boil on buttocks"
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a wrapping resembling a boil, accompanied by softening of the joints; when the patient moves, it causes him to cry out. And the treatment for this illness is as fearful as the one mentioned above. Nevertheless, we shall tell you its workings according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on an elevated seat. Then place the suspension band for the joints below your elbows, around all of the vessels close to the genitals, and stretch them taut. Cut through the scrotum with a broad, sharp scalpel across the vessels until they are exposed. Scrape each side as we have described in the extraction of arteries from the temples. Then insert a needle with double thread where the vessel first appeared and tie it at its first position, then tie it again on the other end. Cut through the middle straightly along the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures. Then treat the wound as others are treated when they have been wounded by an arrow, so that no vessels break open to nourish one of the testicles. For if all vessels become filled with blood, then it is necessary to draw out both testicles from all vessels, so that the seed does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and let them dry and be unable to help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	"Treatment for a broken nose:"
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this ailment come from the cutting that occurs at the bladder or from the stretching above the belly in the area of the hip joints, which causes the intestines to descend from that opening into one of the hips; and this opening is either in the bladder or from the stretching of it, and these two kinds of causes arise often: from blows, jumps, falls, lifts of heavy loads, and similar things; and the sign when it's from the stretching of the bladder is that it happens little by little over a long time, not suddenly; and the abscesses are even unto the depth, for the bladder presses upon the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	"And the signs that it is a fracture of the nasal bone itself are that there is sudden pain at the onset, and there is diverse swelling apparent under the skin, due to the escape of intestinal contents through the defect in the nasal bone."
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	"And sometimes the intestines may descend with the fracture and become trapped in it, causing great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed upon."
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	"And these fractures of the nasal bone require careful handling so that they do not happen frequently due to poor treatment."
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	The manner of this operation is that you should command the patient to insert their intestines by hand into the wound if they can reach it; then hold them on their neck between your hands and lift the thighs; then raise the heart above, and cut all the skin from the long bones; then place the tongues of the hip belt hooks according to what is needed to open the wound, and let them be such that the bladder may issue forth; then scrape off the bladder that is under the skin of the hips until the hard white bladder is exposed on all sides; then insert your right index finger into that which extends from the hip bone, in that which is between the white bladder that is under the skin of the testicle and between the second bladder, and separate that which is behind the testicle and between the second bladder; and then move your right hand inside the hip bone, and raise the white bladder upwards with your left hand, and lift the testicle along with all the bladder towards the hips; and command the assistant to stretch the testicle upwards and release that which is behind the ligature; and search with both hands if there is any intestines wrapped around the hard white bladder, and if you find anything, put it back into the belly beneath; then take a needle with one thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the back part of the bladder, after the hip bone, then cut the ends of the threads that appear until there are four left; then gather them together in the manner of a cross and tie the bladder that we have spoken about which is under the skin of the hips with two strong knots; then wrap up the ends of the threads and tie them tightly on both sides so that none of the vessels may enter inside, lest an abscess come there; and put the knot again according to the first knot long two fingers from it, and after these two knots leave some part of the bladder that is under the hip bone for a handbreadth; and after all this, cut in the part that is under the skin of the hips until the blood flows, and the bowel as we have said above; then bring moist wool dipped in oil and put it on the wounds, and bring the ligature that we have spoken about.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	"And sometimes it may be necessary to cauterize the exposed nasal bone after the incision has been made in case of any bleeding."
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, leaving the joint until it falls by itself; and if it delays in falling, then be aroused with hot water, and place what we have said upon it until it falls; then heal the wound with another remedy until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Here is the translation of the given text with a focus on the term "hernie carnosous":
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this art I have never seen anyone dare to perform a cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch which is bound around the wrist, in such a manner that you bind the vessels, after cutting slightly above lightly on the underside; then cut in the middle, and heal the abscess that opens until the vessels fall; and heal it as we have said until it is healed.
