Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No wound comes from the angles, as we have said, and opens the place; and no intestine descends to the joints, but if any do descend, it is little, and repair all hours; and nevertheless if it remains too long in this point, the wound swells or becomes syphac, until the intestines descend; and this happens by the extension of the syphac that is at the angles, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swollen the place and opens; and its cure is by cautery, as we have before said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: And let the patient lie often on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the wound swollen with the width according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphac that is under the skin that is usual, then take the rod and put it upon the apparent place of the syphac; and press it deep into the belly, then cut the two apparent places of the syphac on the head of the rod, and cut one and the other; then extract the head of the rod, and do not cut the syphac nor extend the wound nor anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestine; then heal it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and heal the wound until it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The infection is confined, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization should be performed more gently at this place, and closer to saving the patient's life.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Regarding the softening of the skin of the thighs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the thighs becomes softened in some men because the flesh that is inside is softened, and it is unpleasant to see. And it is necessary, when one wants to heal it, for the sick person to lie on their back, and cut off the softened skin from the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you wish, first sew up the excess of the softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the sutures, and heal it as one would other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	Regarding castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	And know that castration is prohibited in our law, and therefore I would like not to speak of it in this book; however, it is necessary to mention two reasons for it: one being that the surgeon should be able to respond when asked about it and its cure; and the other because we often have need of castrating certain beasts to aid us, such as bulls, sheep, goats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we use by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water until its testicles are softened and drooping; then grasp them with your hand until they return to their place and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Regarding castration by cutting: you must first tie the beast down, then press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then attach the suspender and cut each cord once after you have thoroughly scraped them. Leave a small piece of the spermatic cord and the delicate spermatic cord that is above the vessels. This method of castration is quicker than that done by attraction because no remnants of the testicles remain to cause the beast to desire lust. Then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	Regarding hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Heraphroditism occurs in two ways among men: one way is that between the two testicles opens also like the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes it dribbles urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way occurs in women: they have upon the pubic hair both like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away all adjoining skin, and cure it as other wounds; but in the second manner, for those men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no remedy.
de la tentigene	Tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is an adjoining skin on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you shave the excess skin of the tentigene with your hand or scissors, and cut it lightly; but do not go too deep lest blood flow, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed. And there is another skin that grows at the mouth of the womb, the armpit, and sometimes breaks out in pustules, resembling a cow's udder, hence the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you bind it, as we have said regarding tenting, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	Erratique
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	The womb is irregular if the nature of the woman is not pierced, or if the opening is small; and it is either congenital or acquired due to illness; or it occurs due to adhering flesh, thin or thick membrane, and it extends deep into the marrow, or on the sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception and childbirth, sometimes also preventing menstruation; and its diagnosis is made by examining the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the inflammation appears nearby, then seek it in your two ears or in your throat.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is due to thin membrane and it appears in both hips, then act swiftly as follows: place your two index fingers together, with the woman lying on her back and her legs spread; then press the two hips firmly until the thin membrane is taut and covers the inflammation; then take wool soaked in oil and apply it to the spot, and have the woman lie facing down each day so that it cannot dry out.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the shoulder blade is hard and thick, then you must cut it like a bay leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is flesh-born, suspend it with garlic and cut it; and have medicinal bandages to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense mixed with egg white; then apply a broad bandage of lead so that the wound does not heal; and do so for a long time, applying a clean linen cloth; then treat with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh-born matter comes in the wound, it must be cut according to this manner, unless it is an incurable abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an incurable abscess that is in the wound, one should not cauterize with fire.
des emorroides	Emorroides est une maladie de la partie postérieure de l’anus et du périnée, causée par une dilatation veineuse ou un hémorragie de ces veines. Les symptômes incluent le saignement lors de la défécation, la douleur dans la région anale, et des masses dures à cet endroit.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are abnormal openings of veins, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard. We have already said in the division their similarities, signs, and now I will say those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are buried deep in the marrow, and they cannot be felt, then there is no cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, those can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold house, then stretch out the piles with forceps, and cut them at their roots, then apply powder containing medicines that constrain blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, then seat her in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and celery seed, and make a plaster with it to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she bleeds, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without cutting; then take linen, moisten it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply it to the location.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ripe, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called 'albathir' is red, and resembles a harsh head, so it should be covered as I have said above; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of boils of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess occur in the martyrdom (i.e., the genitals), such as chancre, pierced abscess, herpes, erysipelas, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in their categories.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the genitals, which is not one of those that boil; and if you wish to know how to work with iron, look to see if the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its appearance, and filled with heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but make it enter until the pain subsides. Then have the patient sit on a seat, and arrange two small seats for them to lean on, and support their back and assemble their feet towards the thigh; and let their thighs be spread apart, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them securely with a good tie. Then suck the bag towards the right side, and bring the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the wound, about which there will come later its form. And it is necessary that when you prepare this instrument, you first insert the rod to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters does not go deeper than it should, and does not injure the patient. And if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the wound with bandages, so that the instrument does not hurt. And it is necessary that they place the horn of the instrument above, and wet the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and it is cut with a soft hand, then it must be covered at its head, on the left side of the spatula; and when the bowel is empty, then you must put moistened tents into the wound in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the tent far from the wound at the bottom of the marrow, and place behind it on the marrow and on the linen cloth moistened with water where mallows have been cooked; then after two days of suitable ointment, until it is healed; and sometimes the marrow and the wound are raised by an enema of water and honey, and then water in which lily roots and long celery have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is in the marrow, you must beware of cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first at the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman hurry downwards and desire to smell the aroma: then the child hastens to come out; therefore know that this birth is according to nature's figure, and the head appears first, with the membranes along with it. And when you see these signs, then press her belly gently so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends on its head, then the membranes are with it, and the marrow is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing. And he who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Sometimes it happens that it comes upon his feet, and fire comes to the body or shoulder, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, sometimes, and is turned by chance over his neck, and in other ugly shapes; therefore, it is necessary for the physician to be wise and subtle in these matters, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the forms how one should help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes on its head through natural issuance, and the woman labors with grief, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a stool, or let women hold her; and arouse her nature with oil of olive or fenugreek cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the little spatumile of which here is the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the amniotic sac, and scrape with its nail until the moisture inside comes out; and take the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must give the woman an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil. Then make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out first, then you must gently push them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high. Then tilt the seat down onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not slip during tilting. And if the hands still cannot enter and the child dies, then cut the hands at the joint that is mentioned here, and extract the child, and reset them evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the birth of a child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out onto its feet, it should be pushed up; then gently turn it little by little until it is even; then take one of the feet and stretch it gently little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to its hips, instruct them to hold it and make it sneeze with some condition; if it jumps afterwards, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he cannot jump as we have said, then turn it bit by bit until it is in its natural shape
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easy
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take musk from a mule's head, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in one mortar; and put this ointment on the woman's nature, then let her sit in warm water up to her chest; and when she is moistened underneath, put a collyrium of myrrh under her and leave it for an hour; then let her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the outlet of the child onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, then the midwife puts her hands softly and gently; then she supports it on its neck, and its feet hang down, and it lies on the bed; and folds its hands softly and gently, and then places its hands on its belly, and removes the pillows underneath so that it hangs down properly; and if the child does not slip out, then take its feet and move it vigorously, then move its belly upwards, then place your hands there; and ease the child out softly and gently; and tell the woman to push until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the outlet of the child who comes from the thigh, keep one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to attempt to replace the hand: if it cannot be replaced, then make the woman stand up and walk away. If she cannot walk away, make her lie on the bed and bend her legs vigorously; then prepare the musciliary as I have described; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then attempt to replace the hand. And bring out the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command the woman to push until the child comes out properly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the outlet of the child on his neck, with his hands spread out and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bath attendant take his hand, then turn it little by little, and wipe it gently; and when it is even, then put on the natural musk of aloe and oil, as we have said, then command her to move little by little; and when you have done this, then make her sit on the seat, and command her to sneeze; and let her yawn.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When heat comes in this manner to the entire amniotic sac, then cut the amniotic sac with your thumbnail until all moisture is expelled; and if the child's face and neck are bent, then cut from the chin so that it is not retained, and the child dies. Then place the child inside, so that you have put it in as it ought to be, and command the woman to push several times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the outlet of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, although it happens rarely
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	There are two strange things that do not live unless given a name; I know of these, which can be multiplied, and are desired by the Sybil who divides them, which is attached to the chin. Sometimes they also come out naturally like everyone else, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out screaming, treat them as we have said, and let the surgeon be skillful, and do quickly and easily what she does; and do thus as it is appropriate to move towards health.
de plusors enfans	Of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	At times they are formed in the uterus I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or even more up to XV, and all are formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the sagacious sage, and it is necessary that the surgeon knows all this, for by chance such things happen; so act accordingly as it is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and if nothing comes out, and you are constrained by necessity to use your hands; it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of sound virtue, and does not have an accident or fears death; then the woman must be propped up on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the assistant should tie two cloths around her, or she should be tied to the bed so that she does not slip during the delivery of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oil containing musk, aloe, fenugreek, and linseed, then the surgeon should coat his hands with these oils and musks; then insert them into the womb gently, then choose one of the places where it is customary to place the hook, and be careful that the child descends headfirst; then insert the hook into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or near the genitals or close to the ribs, and if the descent is on its feet, insert it under the buttocks and midway along the sides; and it is necessary that you hold the hook in your right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of your left hand, and gently press with your whole hand, and insert the hook into any of these places that we have mentioned, until you reach the empty space; this is the shape of the hook.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then thrust against the other bone, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; then stretch them evenly by moving from one side and the other, for easy removal, and let the bones' teeth hold for movement.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some part remains, then the surgeon applies some of his two fingers with oil to that part and presses them in, and draws out the other part; and if none remains, then place this bone higher up and continue until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to stiffness, then you must wrap the cloth all around it until it goes out completely; then cut at the joint of the sole or on the side, and do the same for the other foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and stuck at the exit, or has a sharp-pointed bone assembled there, then you must insert the spatula between your fingers, cut the bone, and remove the point; or grind it with the tool called "almidach," of which the form comes with the tools in the chapter that follows this one; and do the same if the child has a large head naturally. Then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head still sticks and is stuck by force, then cut until the moistures exit from the hip joint; and if it cannot come out, then cut piece by piece as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	"And if the child is on its feet, then traction is easy, and directing towards the mouth of the matrix is also easy."
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or breast, then you must pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut open the belly or breast until the moisture that is there runs off; and if the other members are removed but the head remains, then place your hand deep into the wound, and draw it up to the mouth of the wound; then insert one or two fingers, and pull it out firmly; and if the mouth of the wound is constricted by a hot abscess that has come there, then do not work on it, rather bring moist and fatty things, and with those plaster it up, and soak in softening and moistening waters.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is lying on its side and you cannot make it lie flat, then treat it as we have said for a living child; but if one lacks power to do so, then pull it out by pieces and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the conditions that we have mentioned occur in wounds; and if flows of blood come forth, they should be restrained with water, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose womb contained an infant that had died, then another infant became lodged on top of it and also died
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed inflammation in her vulva which swelled so much that it opened up and began to emit a foul odor
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat her, but after pondering for a long time, I could not heal the wound
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attracting plaster and an bone emerged, then after several days another one appeared
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished by this, for the womb has no bones
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I concluded that they were bones from a dead infant
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and pulled out many bones until the woman was much better. The woman lived a long time like this, but sometimes a little bone came out of its place; and I recorded this chapter for this reason: whenever masters find something strange, they should know how to apply aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	"to bring the dislocation back into place"
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the shape of the presser, to which one applies the books; and at two turns for each of the two heads of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle for the restraint and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be two fingers wide, and its thickness two fingers, and one and a half palms long. And there should be two joints of this same wood between them, which are fastened at both ends, half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the wound to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling the shape of forceps; and it should have two heads with two joints each, about a palm's length long and two fingers wide. When you wish to open the mouth with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, with her feet dangling and legs spread apart. Then insert the two heads of the instrument together into the mouth, holding the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs. Then open your hand fully with the instrument, as you would with equal-sized forceps, according to how much you wish to open the mouth of the marris (vagina), until she is satisfied.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	"These instruments are all mounted, and their appearances are multiplied. When the surgeon has prepared them, the operation is performed more quickly, and the instruments are taller for men because of their size."
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	"Do not disdain the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is not excusable."
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with condimentum (an aromatic substance), holding your hands over her mouth and nose. If she coughs as a result, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, then take the pot and make a hole in its lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marble vase into it, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomille, cassialigne, and centory; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water in the pot over the fire; then place one end of a cane in the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marble vase, and let it steam until the vapors come into the vase; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	"If the membranes are expelled quickly."
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if after this treatment she remains and does not sneeze, then command the maidservant to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in musk from almonds, and then insert it into the vase, and search for the second part. And when she has found it, grasp it gently and pull it out straightly, so that the marble vase does not fall during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pulled out. So it will come out and become loose.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is too narrow, we have said the cure for sneezing and fumigation with herbs. And if it does not improve from all that we have said, then ensure you do not cause harm while treating; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the womb be tied to the woman's hip, then perform a clyster with tetrafarmacon oil. She will be able to urinate and pass through, and there will be heat. But nevertheless, when she does so, an unpleasant odor may come from the stomach and head, causing injury to the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Therefore, suitable fumigations must be used for this purpose. None of the ancients have proven fumigation with watercress and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman during the retention of the flowers and membranes is as follows:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles the skin of a dog, and one places the head carefully over the fire, with wide-open jaws. And let there be fumigation on the coals, until the tinder is wasted, then begin again.
de percier lou fondement	"to pierce the anus"
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born whose anus is not pierced but plugged by a skillful surgeon. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this syfac with her finger and not cut with a sharp instrument, and guard against touching the wound. Then place moist wool soaked in wine and oil on it, until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	"And if you doubt that it has not healed, then place a tube of lead in the opening and leave it there for a few days, removing it when the child is ready to be taken to its room."
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	"Sometimes this obstruction occurs suddenly due to a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cut off that growth: it should be cured as we have said for the lead tube."
de la fistule dou fondement	"of the fistula of the anus"
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come beneath the fundament are nodose, and swellings that come alongside the fundament defected, or in the space of the two parts, so there is one fistula or many; and when this nodosity is ancient, it acts up, and increases moist heat, causing white or subtle bowels, and sometimes these fistulas are persisting; and they are known by those who see them exit with evacuation or windiness when the patient makes evacuation, and sometimes one appears.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	"And there are fistulas that pierce up to the bladder and up to half of the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint and up to the knee."
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes the persistent fistula at the fundament, and not persistent; and it is that you place your two index fingers on the fundament, and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a thin reed of lead or horse hair until you feel the reed or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, nor does evacuation or windiness come from the hole, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; so hurry to heal.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when the fistula is perforating up to the bladder or up to the urethra, urine comes out of it and cannot be healed by medications."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces through to the hip joint, then the tendon comes all the way there. If there is no torsion and inflammation does not spread around, it will pass on its own; there's no need for medicine or immediate ointment in such fistulas. Only labor has power over them, and vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those fistulas that are not yet persistent or old, there is hope for healing by iron. Thus, have the patient lie face down in your hands on their back; lift their legs up to their hips and tilt them towards their belly. Then insert a red-hot iron rod, or one of lead if there's torsion, until you find where the fistula comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around their anus, you must insert your two index fingers into it. If you feel that the fistula has pierced through there, uncover where you sense between your fingers the opening or flesh. Then know that it is persistent; do not work on it unless you can heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	People say it's possible to heal some, but this happens rarely. The aid given there involves heating the cautery iron according to the width of the fistula, as previously mentioned; and inserting it hot into the fistula until it reaches near the fundament; do this twice or three times until you know that those broken tissues have been burned, which resemble a bird's feather; then treat with soft bandages moistened in butter until that charred tissue falls off, then treat with ointment between skin and wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed thus, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this does not heal otherwise; and if the bandage enters but does not pierce to the fundament, and there is a thick layer of flesh or skin between your two fingers and the bandage, and you see the fistula through that covering on the heart side; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and immediately push the bandage forward, and then apply the cautery until it reaches the head of the bandage; and the bandage will be released, and it will fall off; then scrape away those burned tissues which resemble a bird's feather, leaving none remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"If the sinew breaks and tears between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or strong medicine."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the burning of these adjacent hairs, and the extraction of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat wet wounds with butter or crushed plants until the wound gapes open, and have burnt hair removed from the wound; then treat the wound with rubbing ointments to penetrate hard flesh, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is cauterized in this way, it is truly cured and does not return."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if the fistula comes right down from the fundament and is far from the body, push your thumb into the fundament and search for it."
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the wound, and between two there is cloth or skin or hair where it is about to burst, then let there be fire only with trust and hope, by administering one of these three ways: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut until deep, or if you cannot do so put ointments on it and treat it as before; but do not go too deeply lest you cut the tissue that holds the fundament, causing unwanted evacuations. Then treat it as we have said. Perhaps it will be healed, or you may remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut near the fundament, either with ointment or another pointed instrument. Then clean the torn skin in the wound as much as possible; then strive to close the wound and keep the fistula away from the fundament: this will make things easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: when you insert a tube into the fistula and it is located on the side near the foundation of the skin above, then take another tube pierced at the top like this:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	"And tie one end of a thread to the top of the tent, then insert the tent all the way into the fistula until it reaches its tip."
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it pierces into the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that hole so you can insert your finger into the foundation. Then pull the head of the thread and bring the two holes together, tying them tightly to each other and leaving them for one or two days. Sometimes tighten again until the threads cut through those tissues that are between them and fall off. Then heal the wound until it is closed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	"If the fistula does not burst open on its own, make it do so by any means you can, unless it is too deep."
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"For it would not be good to cut too deeply and then treat it as we have described until it is healed;"
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine-like instrument used to open a fistula is very sharp at one end and cutting, but not at the other end, so that it does not cut what should not be cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	"hemorrhoids"
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they constantly emit blood. There may be one or more, and some are defecated along with feces while others are expelled from the anus. But those that are defecated have a little moisture, and sometimes they emit a little yellowish water or a little blood, having the color of flesh. The treatment for those who have hemorrhoids inside the foundation is to advise the patient to strain themselves while going to the bathroom until the hemorrhoids come out, then grasp them with forceps, or hold them with your fingernail, and cut them at their root. If they cannot be held due to moisture, take them with a piece of cloth or cotton, or with a piece of chamois leather, and remove them using both hands, then cut them and apply some warm powders in place of cauterization; or cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter on cautery, until they are healed. If the hemorrhoids cannot come out, then cleanse the patient with a strong and sharp clyster to wash what is inside the anus so that it can come out freely. When the patient strains and if the hemorrhoids have come out of the anus, the treatment is simple: grasp them with your fingernail or forceps, cut them, then heal them as we have said, until they are healed and there is no fear of incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should stitch according to this manner: Take one thread of wool, and pass it through a needle, then pull the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and twist both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and tie the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then place upon the foundation one cloth moistened in rose oil or wax, and place it upon the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rest; and then let him lie until they fall out, and when they have fallen out, then treat them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	"For the drying of the fissure in the fundament:"
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	"Often times a fissure occurs in the intestines due to drying, and this can happen naturally or when the patient is old and medication is ineffective."
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must first scrape off the bark using a sharp tool or your nail so that it does not become moistened. Then treat it until it is healed as necessary. And if it cannot heal, then begin scraping again more vigorously than before, until it is completely scraped and healed. Then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	"For trembling:"
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Little ants appear before the body, and go very deep; sometimes they are felt cold, and the shivering is perceived like death coming into all the body, more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	The cure is to take a quill of goose feather or a strongulture feather, and place it on the shivering so that the circle encircles the shivering entirely; then turn your hand around the entire feather until you grasp all around the shivering, and push it deep inside, and remove the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	"And if you wish to do this with a feather of brass or iron, then do it in this manner, and make sure that it is thin underneath and sharp above:"
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	"Do not pierce too deeply so as not to hurt the fingers or cause them to bleed. And if you wish, cauterize the trembling area, just as it is described in the chapter on cautery."
de la forme dou clistere	"Of the form of a clyster:"
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	"Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or lead, or molten brass or wax; and sometimes they are made of these small or large instruments, according to their size."
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	"Therefore, those that are used for the treatment of children and those who are weak and sickly should be small;"
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	"The form of a small or large clyster is as follows: wide where the belly is bound according to this manner:"
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a discomfort where the belly is bound and pierced from within; and it has two holes on one side, and one hole on the other; and the belly where medicines are placed should be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one span of space; then put a strong thread of twisted hemp through these holes in an X shape or wound around them, and gather the belly like a goat's stomach; and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong string at the front, then administer the clyster.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medication not be too hot nor too cold. Anoint the head of the clyster with oil or donkey's wool, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the servant squeezes it with both hands until it is entirely empty, then remove the clyster and have the patient raise their legs at the side, and if the medication wishes to exit, let it do so as much as possible; and if it remains overnight, that is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if you perform a clyster in an illness where the belly is inflamed and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until it is healed."
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or on an abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child. This is the form of the thin clyster on which the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	"We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines according to their fulfillment."
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	"I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and what they are made with."
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by stone impact and cuts from sword or knife, lance or club or dart, or similar things; or those that are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound falling on the neck, head, face, belly, liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, you should be mindful whether it was caused by a blow from stone or similar objects. If the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt the raising of a hot abscess: then rinse it immediately with cold water if there is any blood flowing from the wound; let the rinsing be on the opposite side of the injured part. Ensure that the patient has fasted from wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it will not rinse, then thin down his diet and let him abstain from wine and meat. And place upon the wound, if a hot abscess forms, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine. And if there is no hot abscess, then apply powder (which I shall mention later) to the fresh wound, ensuring it does not become inflamed by exposure to air; and if inflammation has already occurred, then apply ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like one from a sword cut and similar ones, and its lips cannot be brought together by binding alone, then bring them together by stitching, as I shall say regarding wounds of the belly, concerning stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and hangs open, barely attached, cut it off; then treat the wound with medicine and replace hard skin in place of leather, instructing the patient to eat substantial foods like testicles, cooked wheat, also poultry and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rottenness in the leather and it has no attachment to the bone, cut off all the rot and throw it out, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that does not stop bleeding without a bandage, locate the artery and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then their care is easy; you should place in this powder which binds before the art has moved it
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind them finely into a powder, then fill the wound with it and press it firmly until it blends well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly and do not remove the medicine until the wound is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Sometimes heat alone is applied when incense or dragon's blood are not available, but only after the art has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, especially in summer, do not apply this powder but instead use some digested ointments or poultices made from barley flour, water, and honey until it weeps; then heal with other remedies until it is clean.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture accompanies the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	"of the neck wound"
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	"If a wound comes on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut."
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.
