If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave it alone and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medication be warm, such as warm water washed in honey and mixed with rose oil, and cooked vegetables also washed in warm water, and other similar medicines according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the wound is large, then suture and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals."
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of bowels, then pierce it lower down; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows abundantly, then drain it, tie it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the heart, and the windpipe is guarded, by which the flesh goes, then hold the heart over the canal of the neck, and do not touch the neck but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it tightly, and leave it for a few days, then cure it with drying ointments until it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it out; and if there are pieces of bone, throw them all away if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound rots, and let the sore be drained and closed up; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	"And if there are bones and fistulas in the wound, then treat it as I said in its chapter."
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	"on wounds from a lance or a dagger"
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then observe if wind escapes from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal. And if it is not deep but fresh with all its blood, then do not apply powder at the first hour nor bind it so that the blood does not go deep to the heart and kill the patient; but apply attracting ointment, binding twice a day. And if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days or four or more. Then there will be no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart nor restraints on breathing. And when you see good conditions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Therefore treat it with dressings and other treatments until it is healed. And if it cannot heal but opens again, know that there is a fistula; treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut made by a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the chest or back, then its treatment is with what comes before; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder. And if it has eaten into the bone, and has pieces of it, then examine the wound, and treat any displaced splinters if they are exposed; and if they are not exposed, allow the wound to fester until extraction becomes easier. The judgment for other wounds on other limbs is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	"on rupture of the abdomen"
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And the rupture of the belly can be large, medium or small. Sometimes a large wound causes the intestines to protrude, or a piece of intestine to come out through it, making stitching difficult. A smaller wound may sometimes be worse than a larger one because, when sewing, one must carefully place the intestines back in little by little; but sometimes they swell up quickly from the cold and slip back in more easily. And know that there are four ways to suture the belly: two common sutures happen during abdominal surgery, while two others specific to other wounds on the body occur elsewhere; but these are still most commonly used with abdominal suturing, each of which I will explain and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines has been cut off, and it seems difficult to reset, this can be done in one of two ways: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner: moisten a sponge or one cloth with lukewarm water only, or cook in boiling water cinnamon and cumin and spikenard, and apply the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this wine restraint, and it should be moved with care to desenflame.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, moisten the intestines with water or old honey that has been cooked, for by this the entrance is enlarged little by little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used to remove hemorrhoids; and the first cure should be gentle, so that no one cuts without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: cut inside the curve and do not cut deep, and here is its form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, then carefully replace them according to their natural form in their proper place if you have the power, for this is worth more.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then you should make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, so arrange it that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus should be arranged for both large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, do thus: first prepare what you have at hand, then take a pitiful helper who carefully takes hold of the entire wound with their hand and brings together its lips; and this is the common way of stitching. Take one or more needles according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave two threads of thread from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle with a strong good thread into it. Pierce both heads of the skin with the two heads of the sinew that is beneath the skin inside, until you have pierced them on this side, and gather together the two heads of the sinew with four together; then tie a double thread around the needle on both sides, then join together the two edges of the wound neatly, and leave two threads of thread, and insert another needle into it. Then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and continue to do this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is closed; and let the needles be medium, between fine and coarse, for too-fine needles cut all the flesh, and too-coarse ones cannot enter very well: therefore they must be medium. Do not stick the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it has healed; then cut off the heads of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put lint or bandages on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This way of stitching with needles is more useful for small wounds, because it suffices with one or two needles. The second stitching method is common: gather together both heads of the skin and both heads of the sinew with a needle that has a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these heads all four together, then bring back the needle to the part where you began, in the manner one sews cloth; and put the thickness of a finger's width of thread between each stitch. This stitching is known to men, and I once sewed up a wound on a man's belly who had been cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's length long, and the intestines were coming out well two palms' lengths, and the wound was in his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I reset the intestines after it had been twenty-four hours since the blow, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, which I dressed, and it remained healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	The doctors had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle. I did not dress the wound with any ointment or medicine because there were none available where I was; instead, twice a day I applied old cotton to the wound and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two proper ways to suture: Take the needle and insert it from the outer part until it pierces the heart straight through. Then take the thread on which you inserted the needle, and make it pass through again from the inner part to the outer part. The purpose of this stitch is to sew like a furrier sews furs, leaving one side of the thread once before taking it up again on the other side until the entire suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which Galen discusses distinctly, is as follows: some people join the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the sinew to the other in this way: insert a needle into the nearby end of the muscle, pierce only that spot, leaving both ends of the sinew; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside towards the inside at both ends of the sinew; finally, pierce both on the outside going towards the inside through two other nearby muscles on the opposite side. This is the correct manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some witness it: one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be placed on one side, the other on the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew hides. Know that when the wound is inside the belly, the stitching is more urgent than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood before it has moved, put back the intestines and close the skin; then place powder made from boiled grass on it, and if it has moved, apply some ointment available until the wound closes. Then stitch the wound, ensure the threads are sound, and dress it with bandages and compresses. Then treat the wound like others until it heals. If you don't have medicines, put cotton wool on it as soon as it starts to close, and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But in many cases where wounds are simple, you have no need for other medicines. And if you doubt that the wound communicates with principal members, you should moisten light linen in warm tempered oil or rose oil and place it around the angles and under the armpits. If there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which happens often, wash it out with hot black wine enema. And if putrefaction reaches the intestines, pierce them inside and know that when it's the large intestine, it's easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	Injuries to the intestines called 'jejunum' cannot heal, due to the thinness of their vessels and the delicacy of the entire body, and their closeness in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the nerve jumps out of the wound, put it back in place immediately after the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or greenish-black, you should tie off the area that is black to prevent any blood flow, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the ligature, and place the two ends of the nerve hanging down from below the wound until it falls out to facilitate extraction.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I saw one man wounded in the belly with a lance; the wound was to the right of the stomach, became funnel-shaped and turned into a fistula, through which digestion and wind escaped. I treated it according to what I could, and did not cease refining until he was healed, and the places joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient might have evil in his belly; and there was no evil, but remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when it has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take frogs with large heads, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the frog has opened its mouth, put it on the two lips, so that it draws its mouth open; and then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot untie itself, then put another frog afterwards in this manner that before, until the wound is entirely covered; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These heads also happen in the intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, like this: take the head of this intestinal string that is very skinned, and then tie at the head of this string a thin twisted linen thread, then put the string into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and join it in the opening; and this manner of sewing with frogs is no further than according to the way of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is neither device nor healing, but only thinness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	"whether it is a fistula or wherever it may be,"
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows large, is universally called "fistula," and likewise when it becomes hollow and sinks inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is truly a ruptured and whitish nodule, where no pain is felt, and it is also hollow like the feathers of a bird; sometimes clear and deep, sometimes thick; sometimes small, sometimes large enough. I have already spoken about this in the section on wounds, that any wound which does not heal has flesh only because of one of nine causes: namely, either because of the smallness or badness of the blood or body, or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips that does not allow flesh to form, or because there is too much depth, or the location is putrid, and the material is of poor quality, or the medicine used in treatment was not good, or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature, or because the property of the region is tardy in digestion and slow in healing by nature, or because there are veins or bones present. I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and their remedies for medicines in that section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	"Now it is fitting that I tell you about the cure of fistula which is done by manual work:"
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas which come from the great veins, and the arteries, and the nerves, or to the spleen, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and there are such that come to the property of the principal member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing else but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula which does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know well how to recognize it, then take a tent of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, so seek it; and if the fistula is crooked, so search it with a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends more around the crookedness; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings, for moisture will pass from one opening to another, and cleanse it. Then seek it with your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and how deep it goes, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel at the pressure of your hand, and where they feel it. And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut it according to what I have said, and remove the fault and the corrupt flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healthy, and if the fistula is very deep on the right side, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then put moistened tents in hot water medicine, and place them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrode the superfluity that remains at the bottom. Then put healing ointments made from fresh meat, until it is healed. And if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt because of the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not trouble the principal member as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then wait until all the corruption is removed, then treat the surrounding flesh until it is clean; and if it is not clean, and still bows like before, know that you have not gone deep enough: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it is thus cleaned, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	But if not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; so there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature. And if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can grasp it with tongs, then extract it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, and if there are many bones, then cut them all, leaving none behind. And if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then cut away the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place something irritating to rot on the wound, and let it remain until the flesh is entirely rotted around the bone, and then they will come out more easily; and if it's a large bone like that of the leg or thigh, then continue removing only the corruption until all blackness has been removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much corrupted part reaching close to the bone's marrow, then it must be cut down to the corruption, and then heal it until it is sound; and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in one man's leg, so that you may take example and help from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was once a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg from some cause that came from within the body so much that matter reached the leg and swelled with a large abscess, but there was no opening to release it. But physicians through their folly opened upon the abscesses too much, and corrupted many materials, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared which all flowed bowels and moisture from the body; and many physicians cared for him around two years, yet none skilled in the art of medicine were called until I was summoned, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, and what flowed through the holes in great quantity. The young man's body became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which I found to be corrupted and perforated, with corruption reaching to the inside of the bone. I scraped off what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, believing that there was no other corruption besides what I removed. Then I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal. Afterwards, I began again and discovered the bone as before, finding that the corruption had continued into the bone. I scraped it off and then removed it, intending to mend the place. But even after cutting around about a palm's width of the bone and removing it completely, I could not succeed in mending it. Then I treated it with medicines again, and it became sound and healed quickly. There was no need to recommence the operation except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the purpose of bloodletting was often performed, but he was entirely healed afterwards, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and he was of good disposition and had no harm nor contradiction at all, neither oncoming nor departing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this manner: take linen and tie it at the head of the bone that is open, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and place another thicker linen bandage over the first one, and bind it on the flesh that is above the bone, and pull the rotted flesh below, and uncover the flesh where you see fit, so that the bone does not wound the flesh; and place a hot iron or a heated brick under the bone to move the rotted flesh away; and this should be done as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is decayed and does not appear, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh; then place a brand underneath, and then sew from one side to the other the decay, and let the sewing be as long as the decay of half a foot, as we have said; and if the decay is at the joint, cut off the decayed joint, and sew the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the decay is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other choice but to cut; and if the decay is at the knuckle of the hand or at the knuckle of the foot, that thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you must examine this corruption how it opens; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve does not oppose you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance outside, and their thickness and their fineness, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each type of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; so consider the instrument that you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head rots away either from within or due to lack of use; and when you have treated this decay with medicines but they are ineffective, then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to the point where the decay begins, so that the patient escapes death or the greater evil of loss of limb. The sign of this is that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and afterwards, after the blackening, the decay spreads from limb to limb, affecting the whole body; so you must act quickly. If it is due to the bite of venomous creatures such as sea scorpions or snakes and similar ones, if the decay starts at the tip of a finger, amputate there but do not allow the decay to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, amputate at the joint so that the decay does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, amputate at the elbow. And if it passes beyond the elbow, death is certain, and there are no remedies powerful enough to save the quantity of its strength. And this is how it goes when decay affects the foot: if it reaches the first joint, amputate after the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, amputate the whole foot. And if it spreads up the leg, amputate at the knee joint. And if it rises above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die. The manner of amputation or cauterization of the limb is thus: tie it above and below with two cloths, one downstream from the lower tie and the other upstream from the upper tie, then cut away the flesh that lies between the two ties with a wide-bladed knife until the bone is exposed; then amputate or cauterize, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the cautery does not touch the healthy area and cause further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood flow comes while you are working, hasten to cauterize the place with powders that restrain it; then return to your treatment until it is complete; then bind the wounded limb with an appropriate bandage and tend to it until it heals.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No boil ever comes on delicate flesh and stays so long that it forms a large swelling; then it grows round and pierces through, and the bowels burst forth, leaving the place empty like an earthen vessel. The skin above is as thin as a silk cloth, not reaching to the bone or nerve, and such disease is called 'sain', not 'fistula'; but if it stretches so far that it reaches to the bone and goes deep, then it is called 'fistula'. And the treatment for this is to cut around that skin, even if it is thin like a silk cloth; yet do not be afraid of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin is hardening and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it thus by irrigation: examine if the breast is large, and the bowel that comes from it has a foul odor. Then use Egyptian medicine made like this: Take aloe, oil, and lead ointment in equal parts, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey. Then take some according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and use it for irrigation, inserting it into the breast and closing the opening. Leave the medicine there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the foulness removed. Sometimes use water from ashes for irrigation when Egyptian medicine is not available. Take ash from burned grapewood, add water to it, let it cool, and use it for irrigation until you know that the breast is well cleaned. If the patient cannot tolerate this, nor Egyptian medicine or water from ashes, then use water and honey for irrigation with a little crushed lead ointment added; or use honey mixed with wine, where the honey has properties of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the wound harden. When you have done this, and believe that the breast is well cleaned, then irrigate it with something that produces flesh in it. Take diachylon plaster, melt it with rose oil and wine, or use other medicines and ointments whose properties I have mentioned when treating ointments. If the opening of the breast is small and the tube of the irrigation cannot enter, then enlarge it slightly with an iron tool, insert a tampon of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it becomes enlarged. If the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave only enough space for the irrigation to enter. If the opening that emits bowel is above, then cut below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bowels are deep, do not let any flesh enter; and if you cannot cover the lower side of them as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowels move to the lowest point where they are. For when the bowels are deep, do not let any flesh enter, and if you cannot cover the lower side of them as you see fit, arrange it in this manner: let the bowels move easily downward, and leave nothing of the bowels; and take consolidating medicines to put on the skin, and stretch over it a linen cloth that covers all the skin. Then cut against the entrance of the breastbone about one fingerbreadth wider than the first. Then gently apply ointment onto another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the entrance of the wound to alleviate the bowels, and do not remove the large outer cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the entrance of the breastbone, often remove it to remove the bowels, and know what comes out from the bowels, whether it's venom or little or much, or digested, or undigested. And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not. And when your medicine has been applied in this way and you see how it acts on the entrance of the wound, then know that the breast is already healed, and approaches health. And then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unwrap the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	"And if after many days the breast still discharges undigested bowels, know that the breast has not yet healed."
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are contracted after a long time, do not despair of health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	But there are people whose flesh in their wounds is slow to heal, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food jumps from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach has not emptied itself; and if the stomach is slow to empty, and is distant, apply drying medicines of dry substance and virtue, such as diaphanous ointment, for it contains much vitriol, which is the last medicine; take diaphanous ointment, and they make it with rose oil, and rose vinegar equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and this same thing does better cooked honey when diaphanous ointment is not present, or you can take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, grind them, and powder them on the honey while it is on the fire; then put it on a cloth, and place it on the stomach, and sometimes administer long aristologue, and roots of celestine lily, which is also like flour of wheat and barley; and use simples or composites: grind them, make them into powder, and put them on the honey that I have mentioned, and use them; and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and has made an impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on ligaments; so the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil of the fingernail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the thumb of the hand, or the toe, or sometimes arises in other toes; and when it becomes old and is not taken care of, then there comes a hard, running, and weeping abscess that runs so far as to reach the root of the nail, and sometimes reaches the entire nail; and the corruption reaches down to the bone, such that there comes a foul-smelling pain, and the head of the toe becomes swollen, and its color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is greatly helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; but if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick and fester, then you must place a blade underneath the nail that pierces the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away that subtle and tender flesh gently and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it and draw out fire, for as long as the rotted bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see both rotting, cut it at one of its ends just as was said earlier, then treat it until it is healed; and if it is wounded and inflamed, causing great pain, you must first heal it; then cut off the claw of the thorny spur at an angle across it, and make sure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the claw, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are sometimes found in some men's hands by chance are entirely fleshy, and sometimes there is bone or claw, and sometimes they arise from the root of the joint, where the birth is on some of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with any knot of the two does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the two sometimes moves; the waist of one who is fleshy is light in this manner: cut him at his root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that originate from the root of the joint are difficult to treat: hold down and cut off.`
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born with a hard knot at the shoulder, first you must cut around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then scrape it until it is clean.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The scabs that come on both toes together are caused by birthmarks or scars from wounds or burns or similar things.`
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut that union so that the shoulder blades return to their natural forms; then place between two wet cloths or oiled rags soaked in rose oil, so they do not fuse together; or place between two thin pieces of lead until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If scabs come on any of his toes with the palm, cut off that adhesion as necessary;`
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Wounds are large veins filled with melancholic excesses that come from various parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him sometimes a purge for the colon, and then treat it with the basilica remedy.`
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cautery with iron is done in two ways: one is that you cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you raise the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this way: first raise the leg with very hot water until the thick blood becomes thin, then hold the leg of the patient down from above the hip to just below the knee; then cut the vein at one, two, or three places with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood by hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient's strength can bear; then tie it, and command that they bind with fresh black colophony; and resume evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the veins is done in this way: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut near the vein at the long end of the knee, or below the ankle bone; then cover the skin with oil, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and it will appear red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then place the hook underneath so that it lifts the skin, and then stitch it lightly to an ointment, then cut in another place three fingers up; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the hook as you did before, and stitch it to another ointment, then make another cut if needed, then lift and cut at the two feet, then draw it out and lift until it is all drawn out, then cut again; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then insert a needle with strong doubled thread, and tie and draw it out, and place it under the hook, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and make sure it does not cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be drawn out or lifted, and harm will come to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, then put moistened wool in wine and rose oil on the wound, and dress it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the sinew is contracted and twisted and enfolded together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly but do not sever it completely, and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to cut the sinew is curved and does not cut too deeply, so as not to cut into the vein; it should be thickly curved, for if it were thin it would cut into the vein, but let it be thick as we have said; this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is embedded in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land with no moisture; sometimes it grows elsewhere besides the legs, and this happens due to rot that comes from under the skin, as it happens inside the body with serpents and worms, buried between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that there appears a very large inflammation on the leg, then the location changes, and the vein starts to protrude like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the thigh opens, you must wrap around it a piece of lead from three to two inches wide and tie it on the leg, letting the lead hang down. Each time it leaks at the front, wrap the lead around it again and retie it. If it is too long, cut off one part and wrap the remaining piece, but do not cut it near its root lest it enter the flesh and cause an abscess or corruption in that place, resulting in a bad disease. Therefore, it should be treated gradually up to its head, leaving nothing on the body. Sometimes this vein can stretch five palms long or ten, and once a man came to me whose was ten palms long. When you cut it, insert a knife into the hole and pierce it all the way down so that everything comes out; empty the material inside and bring healing medicines to apply there against corruption for several days before treating it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or in the foot, and there are many perforations from which blood flows profusely; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle sickness," because it often affects oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body moving up and down, and can be felt well as it moves from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaves a trail of pus; and it is caused by corruption of some humors, like worms, serpents, tapeworms, and roundworms in the belly; and its evilness is doubted, because when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can go to the eye, sometimes entering it and destroying the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it curing and drawing forth, then one can only do so when it goes: thus, it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong bandage very tightly. Then cut upon it and draw out the worm, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it can run into the eye, as we have said. And if you see it coming near to the head or close to the eye, press down tightly on it from below with the eyebrow, then cut upon it and draw out the worm. The patient must use bodily cleansing with dissolving medicines for corrupt humors and eat fresh foods that are not rotten.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	due to pain caused by windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land " vakkir ", and it is a pain that comes into certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb. I have seen this with my own eyes.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw something like a worm rise up to the shoulder, quicker than anything, like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout her body, so that she felt it in the other arm; then she told me that she was continually turning around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how she could move thus from limb to limb because I had never seen this disease behave in such a way."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had often seen pain move from one place to another, but never as clearly as I saw it in this woman; and I thought that perhaps the reason was because she had dry skin and visible veins, which caused that constrained windiness to appear; and those who are moist-skinned with concealed veins do not appear thus.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain which we have mentioned, then hasten to apply a plaster above and below, and then cut until that constraint wind escapes from its place; cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then use remedies that relieve winds, such as fetid pills and pills of serpentine, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Sighs are various according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they occur."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The varieties of them are such that there are those which have large points, and small, barbed, and smooth; and those which have two angles, those with tongues, those with fragments; and those which fall into any limb fall in one of two ways: either into a principal limb, such as the head, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.
