When it falls then into any place of these limbs, and the signs of death which I will tell you about appear: then you must beware of the extraction of this arrow, for many deaths follow afterwards; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of an arrowhead when it falls and pierces the bone, and bursts forth the blood that is on the head, is when there occurs scotoma, soddenness, exertion, and redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes there is bleeding from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes one loses speech and voice; and there appears from the wound white moisture resembling feathers, and there also occurs burning of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then take care, and remove the arrowhead if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of an arrow striking the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck into something hard, not empty; and sometimes the arrow moves like a feather, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come on, and fainting occurs: then know for certain that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The signs of a sigh that has entered the lung are that foam comes forth from the wound, the throat swells up, the patient changes color and sighs loudly and asks for cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"And if the sigh enters the covering of the lung, it is near the ribs. There will be much wheezing and great pain, with loud sighs; all the shoulder limbs move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if a sigh falls into the stomach, sometimes undigested food may emerge from the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if a sigh falls into the abdomen and much wind rushes out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery or for drawing out the sigh."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if a sigh falls into the bladder, urine flows forth and there is diarrhea; the patient feels great pain. You should know that the wound is mortal."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"The other limbs such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary limbs, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and similar limbs are safe according to various conditions."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When a sigh is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous (as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise),"
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one that an arrow struck him at the root of his neck; I attempted it and drew it out from beneath the fat of the ear, without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I drew out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the skin, and the arrow was lodged deep; only its tip could be reached towards the wood; it was large like a Turkish bow, made entirely of iron without ears; the eye was healed, and no ill happened to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian; it was Arab-made with ears; I cut off the barbs and carefully removed it until it came out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I drew out an arrow from a man that had fallen into his belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut open the arrow, engaged it, and pulled it out through force, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to help the man upon whom an arrow has fallen on his back, and the wound has healed over it; and the arrow remains within him, and does not change its natural position, nor find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to help another man upon whom an arrow has fallen in his face, and the wound has healed over it; and he remains thus without suffering great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow struck one of the king's servants in his nose, and it fell into his nostrils, leaning somewhat to the right side; and the arrow was entirely buried when I was called for treatment after three days had passed.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt around with all care and did not find it [the arrow]; and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was the tip of the arrow. I placed plaster with digestive poultice on the place to prevent inflammation; and the head of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed my hand over the wound for many days, and reopened the healed scar, and thus the patient felt the arrowhead inside his nose on the first day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days until it opened, and tested it, feeling the tip of the arrowhead pressing against its place; then I applied more of this medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became clearly visible; and after about four months had passed, the wound healed over so much that I could not extract the arrow with forceps; therefore, I did not cease to refine and devise various tools until I finally extracted it one day using well-made forceps, according to what is described at the end of this chapter.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I therefore sutured it, and the wound healed completely, leaving the patient entirely well.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the qualities of extracting certain arrows, so that you focus your care on what I do not mention, for books cannot encompass everything; but a wise master examines even small things, and finds new works and new tools for dealing with unusual events in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows exit from the limbs where they are stuck in one of two ways: either through the point where they entered or through another part; and those which come out through the point where they entered are called flesh-piercing arrows, and sometimes remain sticking.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be until the flesh is softened around it and the exit wound is eased; and likewise if it is stuck in bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for a few days, moving it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, then carefully cut around it with a fine knife until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it stay there for a few days until it becomes even, because if the arrow reaches so deep, death is imminent.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not reach too deep, and the patient remains for a few days without bad symptoms, then attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is very deeply implanted and cannot come out, then apply poultices around it as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healthy."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is buried in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it thoroughly; and if you feel it, pull it out with some appropriate instrument. And if you cannot do so because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins involved, then cut the flesh until the wound is large enough. Then pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrow that prevent its removal, cut away some of the flesh around it, two parts on each side that you can reach, and then break or bend the barbs so that you can pull out the arrow; but be careful not to break the shaft as you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then wait until the place around is properly prepared, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and the vein, and devise how you can gently pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for that is the greatest help. If you cannot do this, then place them according to what the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes from another direction, where some part of it is visible or the skin around it is swollen and can be seen or felt: cut there until you can grasp it with forceps, then pull it out: it will come out more easily now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then resume extraction until it comes out completely; and if the shaft of the arrow is in place, remove it together with the shaft; and if the shaft has broken off and you wish to administer a counter-incision, introduce the surgical instrument carefully so that the tip of the arrow enters into its groove; then push it through, and if the arrowhead has entered the bone, introduce the instrument backwards into its groove to aid extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead has entered, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as it ought.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the foot or belly or bladder or side, and it is nearby, then cut upon it if you can; but guard against cutting the vein and the nerve, then extract it, then suture the wound if necessary; and tend to it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat bones is similar to a bird's beak, and here is an illustration of that shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the bone fragment.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feathers of a bird, for driving into the point of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	Here is the shape of forceps for grasping and pulling:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which bloodletting is performed, of which sixteen are on the head: two branches after the ears called 'dous herbech', and two arteries in the temples; two veins in the corners of the eyes called 'aspires'; one vein in the forehead; one vein at the nose's tip; two jugulars in the neck; two veins above the mouth, known as 'augeherich'.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly known are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it runs along the right side, which unlearned people call "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast", composed of the cephalic and the basilica, which unlearned people call "vein of the heart"; and the basilica runs on the left side, which unlearned people call "vein of the belly", and it lies above the elbow pit, being that which is most openly apparent at the fossa.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, having II branches; and in the leg and foot are III veins: one runs beneath the curve of the left elbow pit, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are III veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins that are behind the ears help in ancient purging and bleeding. The quality of the bloodletting is such that you should raise the patient's head and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth. Then, make the patient strain their neck with a vise, until both veins appear behind the ears at two dependent points on the head. Then feel for the pulse under your thumb, and seize it. Next, take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone. Then raise your hand along the vein upwards, and cut through the skin and the vein well across with two fingers' width, and make blood flow out as much as you can see. Then bind and compress it until it stops bleeding; I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in both temples is beneficial for ancient purging, sodomites, and customary ophthalmia, and for the course of tears from the eyes. And this is how it is done: make the patient strain their neck until both veins appear clearly. Feel for the pulse under your thumb, then seize it firmly. Then raise your hand on top of the vein with your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, raising the vein upwards and cutting through it as you did with the other two veins. Let blood flow according to your necessity. Then release the patient, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton and compress it firmly until it stops bleeding; we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the frontal vein is as useful for old facial diseases and migraines as the cephalic vein; its quality is such that the patient strains their neck while twisting, until the veins appear; then take the tool called "fossor", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein and press down with your hand or something else, allowing as much blood to flow out as you desire; then untwist the patient's neck and tie off the vein until it stops bleeding.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too narrow, and tie it diagonally, because the bone is close by, and sometimes the flame breaks when it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins located in the temples is beneficial for the eyes and against epilepsy, redness, inflammation in the eye, and facial diseases. Its quality is such that the patient strains their neck while twisting, just like before; then bleed them and let the blood flow diagonally, a bit long but not too wide, as there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is too thin, it may break. Then apply pressure to stop the bleeding, until you have enough blood. Then tie cotton on top and tie it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The veins of the nose are useful for fever, and sudden frenzy, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is chronic. And the qualities of the veins are such that the patient strains their neck, then strains their nose towards your left hand, and takes a long, subtle flame, and inserts it between the lips into the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it overnight, for it restores quickly. And this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The veins of both arms help with the extraction of bile, and the beginning of mixing [medicines], and many diseases, and measles, and corrosion, and herpes, and skin conditions. And the qualities of the vein are such that the patient strains their neck downwards on both sides, as we have said; then let the master stand on the head of the patient, who sits on a chair, then cut the long vein a little wide, then draw temperately blood or as much is needed, then do the same in the other vein, then tie the thread and hold gently between the veins so that the patient does not strangle; leave it until morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of bodies
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	"The juice of the veins of the lips above aids in coldness in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and nose and around."
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of healing are such that you should have the patient sit before you, and hold their neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are recognizable by their black color, and by the small black veins around them: therefore cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the largest from each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for they are one and the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healing underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins that are underneath the tongue aids afterwards the healing of the cephalic vein, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth. The qualities of the healer are such that the patient should sit between his hands before the sun, raise the tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: cut both of them, but do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The blood vessels of the arm are commonly opened in two ways: either by pricking with a wide-mouthed lancet, or with an olive-shaped sharp one called "anesil", depending on the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the mirror blow is very well known, and is wide as you see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening hairy veins filled with visible thick blood that contain thick and turbid blood; this is the shape of the olive-shaped lancet.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more pointed and fine, and is for letting the veins that have thin, lemon-colored blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica vein, one of these veins, helps those who are ill in the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen. The bleeder must bleed profusely and beware of the artery that lies beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flows copiously, then it is necessary to staunch it as I said; and the lancet must not be pointed but sharp like an anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilisk does not open visibly, then you must remove it and replace it with another; or if you wish any vein of it, or if you heal in place of it the vein within the arm: it opens visibly; and the tip to the burning flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know how to recognize the location of the vein, then beforehand remove the arm, touch the location until you feel the pulse; then mark the location from above, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the burning flame; and be careful that you do not strike the artery when you see the location swollen, for that is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see something coming out above like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: act quickly then, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm then, and leave it thus, and do not let the patient move it; and be fearful, and do not let them move until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"And if the bleeding does not stop and he faints, and there is no doctor present, then cut the artery if it appears, for its head contracts; and stop the bleeding."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, cut it open, and take one half and tie it firmly in place until the next day. If bleeding stops, that's good; if not, treat it with powders that stop bleeding, as we have said before. The application should not cause harm in many situations due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The wound in the middle of the vein helps by drawing blood from above and below because it is composed of basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said before. The surgeon must be careful not to injure the nerve that lies underneath, especially if puncturing too deeply, which can cause swelling, injury to the sinew, and possibly even prevent healing. This nerve often becomes exposed, but in some men it remains hidden due to its fineness. Therefore, you should treat it with an instrument called an Ansel, and press on the nerve as strongly as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise;"
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein helps, for it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes. It is best to bleed using the olive or myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is important to find the easiest place and not be discouraged if one fails at first; one can try again. Sometimes the spot may swell in some people when bled for the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of letting depends on your judgment."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only performed for the sake of maintaining health and preventing future illnesses. Bleeding should be done in one of these three veins located on the arm: the cephalic, basilic, or median cubital vein. It should be done at the beginning of Lent, in autumn, and in winter after a meal when signs ofpletion appear. One should bleed on the first or third day of the month, two or three hours after noon.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick one who is given medicine for illness has no fixed time for it, but when there is need by day or night, at all hours and at all times; and one must not give medicine to children until they are fourteen years old, nor to a woman carrying fruit except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly over 60 years of age receive this medicine.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to take medicine, in whatever manner it may be, then one must first purge the intestines with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw out the harmful superfluities from the intestines into the principal members; nor should he who is too full of food or drunkenness take medicine until he has fasted for some time. And one must not give medicine after a bout of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, menstruation, hard labor, waking and fasting, or anything that depletes all virtue, either from a blow to the weapon or body. Then subtly refine the humors with foods and drinks and medicines if you have the power to do so; then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood; and let him take medicine from the vein at the elbow on the third day as we have said; and guard that day from labor, hunger, lust, and similar things. Be tied down and joyful, and may the sickness be higher than he who is being sickened, and rub his arms twice or thrice, then hold the lien tightly in the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, then the blood cannot flow correctly; then moisten the medicine with a drop of old oil, then place his thumb from his left hand on that vein beneath where he wishes to take medicine, so that the vein may rise and swell at the striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like strings from the bloodletter, and some such are filled with windiness so that when one places fire on them, they withdraw from the fire and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with many; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the bloodletter must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, that is good. But if not, then begin again a little below or above that place immediately, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen and the patient fears it, let him wait one or two days without tying the arm: perhaps he will have a boil come out; do not enter into baths then restart the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the hole is small, or the blood comes subtly and you doubt that it does not flow much blood as you see, then apply fire to that same hole directly; and work quickly before the place becomes swollen for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the wound swollen, do not recommence the cautery, and put a bit of oil ointment on it, for it lightens the body's blood, and in this place the oil's balm is most effective; and so administer oil ointment in each cautery that you perform on veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and the same effect has turpentine and bowels of ox, when placed upon the wound.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess appears, which happens often especially when the vein was not cauterized well at its first opening, then hurry and place a warm compress of sponge moistened in water on it, keeping it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped. If blackness or greenness remains on the wound after some days, don't worry about it; but if you see fit, apply something made from aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastich, or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an ulcer and appearance appear during the administering of basilica: therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to apply anything that we have spoken of here, for perhaps some blood will flow from the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the place, and then cleanse it with another cleansing until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw off the blood according to each person's constitution and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it issue forth until it becomes red. And if it flows thickly, let it flow until it becomes more subtly flowing. And if it is too hot, let it cool before striking again.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a wider cut be made, and the flame be wide; but for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they should be pricked frequently and gently, and this should be done by incising rather than puncturing; and this method of bleeding prevents excessive loss of blood and damage to nerves, and it is better than long or wide pricking.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body fails to bleed properly, give them dough moistened in pomegranate juice; if they are hot, let three or four bloodlettings be done; and if they are of cold temperament, let them eat before the bloodletting dough moistened in musk syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if they faint during bloodletting, after losing much blood, then they must inhale broth of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have spoken of in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to evacuate one arm and have bloodletting done again afterward, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he be bled a little at a time according to his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to evacuate one arm after the first bloodletting and has a strong body should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to have bloodletting done on another part of the body should be bled on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw out a large quantity of it, and widen the opening so that it flows freely into a basin. Then, after you have prepared all the conditions for healing, and place your hand on the pulse when it heals, ensure that the patient does not come in place of the basin, which happens often if the attendants are negligent; but it is not necessary to tighten the loop around the arm, nor to press strongly the second time when the opening has closed. If the arm is bent, let it extend quickly for it would be bad; but wait until it heals a second time. Or you can cauterize with the tip of the flame so that the blood which is congealed at the mouth of the vein flows out. Then place some salt mixed in water on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	"But if the vein is swollen, do not let go nor squeeze too hard until the inflammation has subsided."
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	"And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, do so either in the same vein or in another one, or even in the other arm."
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	"The vein in the arm is opened in place of the vein in the head because it is more accessible."
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the cautery is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until the vessels become red; then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well. Then the cautery is applied across, not wide nor long. And let the opening be large. And let it be cauterized near the joint of the hand. If blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water and let it bleed into the water until you have enough. But if it's summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for one puts it more often in winter than in summer. And the cautery of this vein is safer than all others because there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cautery for the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver. And this is the manner: constrain the hand and put it in warm water until the vein swells and can be seen. If you cauterize across and cut all around, it will not harm anything. But do not go too deep, because nerves are underneath all bones devoid of flesh. Then put the hand back in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And when you have drawn enough blood, apply oil and a little salt to quickly cauterize the wound, and do this for each cut."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The bleeding of the vein in the left hand is beneficial for those suffering from mumps, and it should be done in the same way as I have described for the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The juice of the soapwort is beneficial for all illnesses below the body, such as those of the womb, retention of fluids, and diseases of the spine, thighs, and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its juice are that the patient boils some of it in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it reddens, and then binds it over the ankle joint. The vein is located at the ankle, and many nerves go up the leg from there; therefore, apply it to where the largest nerve is or at the ankle, as this works best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you bleed on the foot, beware of the nerves that lie beneath. Make the cut across, like cutting a slice; and let the blood flow freely."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, immerse the foot in water again and allow the vein to empty completely."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the juice fails on the first application, then try again a little higher up, as the place may be salty. Do not fear damaging a nerve, as we have said, and apply soapwort to the other leg in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is on the outside ankle, and bleeding it is beneficial for lower back pain when caused by hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its juice are that the patient enters into a bath and holds up their foot with four fingers twisted behind the ankle, as otherwise the vein will not open. And if it opens, then apply the juice in every way you can, including across it. It is better to tie it off afterward because the place is rough and many people have tried this method.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then take any vein that opens on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let the blood flow as much as you see, and then untie the bandage, and place cotton and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	And regarding the applications of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	"Leeches are made from horn, glass, or earthenware and can be used in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking."
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping that is done without cauterization is of two kinds: either it is done with fire or without fire. And cupping that is done by cauterization and bloodletting is performed in fourteen places on the body, among which one is entirely on the forehead; another is in the neck; two others are on each side of the neck; one below the chin; two on the shoulders; two on the hips; two on each arm; two on each leg; two on each ankle. And cupping does not draw blood except for the small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and thus it does not weaken at all, as is done with veinletting. And it should not be administered in any disease caused bypletion, until the entire body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary to bleed due to illness, or for customs, then we will do so each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at all times; for there are those who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head. And there are some who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes. And some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an swollen tongue, and bleed excessively. And there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounded and dead people and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially during the month, we will order them to be leeched three hours after noon."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the veins helps with headache ..., which comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be done after evacuating the entire body; and this bleeding takes the place of bleeding from the head, and those who are of cold complexion or have a cough should not use it, for it does great harm to them. And therefore old people should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful. Therefore, the leech should be placed a little lower to avoid forgetfulness."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The windpipe among the neck is in place of the health of the head and the basilisk, and for that reason it helps in the stretching of the arm, and in splitting open the channel of the lung, and in thirst and in fullness; and there one should put little pressure, for if it holds too firmly, it causes obstruction to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The windpipe between the two ribs of the neck is useful for pains in the head, and for inflammation of the eyes, migraine headaches, strangulation, and pains at the roots of the teeth; it replaces the health of the basilisk. You must command the surgeon that he press his hand gently while placing it, so that he does not strike an artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Windings under the chin are good for mouth disease, gum decay, and similar mouth diseases; and they are located at the entrance of two lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"The shoulder windings are good for diseases that come from heat and swelling."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windpipe from the ribs is as useful as the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from those large veins. Command the surgeon not to strike too deep with his hand, for the place is bare of flesh and has nerves and arteries beneath it.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the buttock is useful for hemorrhoids and lower diseases, and the cupping glass must be large and made of bronze, so that it can draw well; and sometimes if it is too fine, it may break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs draw openly because they attract blood from all over the body and are useful for old pains in the kidneys, sciatica, bladder, and joints; they replace two sophenes and two ankles, but they also weaken the body after prolonged use and cause swelling in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first apply it empty, and suck moderately, then place it quickly and move it evenly without stopping until you see the skin turn red and swollen with blood visible on the surface. Then remove it and replace the cups, taking care to observe the condition of the body because some people have thin flesh and tender pores, so you should strike only once, make the wounds wide but not too deep, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time. And when we want to draw only a little blood at a time, one stroke will suffice.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we begin often; and if the blood is thick, let it be heated deeply, and its end should be such that the heart is suddenly pierced, and it suits those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you oil the places for cups of aperitive and dissolvent oil: if it's in summer, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucurbit seed oil; and if it's in winter, of cress oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excessiveness is thick and cold, use almond oil or balm oil or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if it is for one who has tender flesh and wide pores, then no oil should be put on, but it should be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of morelle, or water of cucurbit, or water of porcellain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should rise using this method: with myrtle water or sumac water and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine or water of succus, or decoction of fennel or camomile, or others similar; and it is not necessary to bleed before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and he should not sleep after bleeding, and it is necessary that he warm himself when he must be bled and when he is bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And let those who are bled be careful if they become choleric, and if the blood is too hot and inflamed; then it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce with oil, and similar things; and eat few pulses, and castrated meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have cold complexion should take honey syrup and medium perfumed wine, which is between old and new, and eat little meat, and few pulses and small birds and poultry; and on the day when he will be bled, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or musk before or after bleeding, to strengthen the main members; and let the blood be subtilized, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Ventouses placed without striking are those placed on the liver, and the womb, and gout, and on the belly and the chest and the loins and the haunch; for these limbs do not suffer being struck upon, nor is it done otherwise than to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them on the breasts when milk is abundant; to remove the viscidity that is in the limb, as we place ventouses on the belly and on the chest to lessen the limb; and it removes pain, when there is obstruction or stone, it may by its attractive virtue draw away the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it does when placed on the liver and on the womb when there is retained windiness, and these ventouses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the ventouse with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and it should have around the middle one small hole, like for putting in a needle, made of brass, softened beforehand so it does not wound the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle it should have a transverse rod of brass or iron to hold an enclosed candle, and there should be both large and small ones according to the illnesses and the size of those who use them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the elderly, and of the thin than the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must place this cupping glass on the limb thus: light the candle of wax or flax and put it inside the cupping glass through the rod that is within the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and ensure that the two fingers are over the hole we mentioned earlier, so that when you wish to do so, steam can escape through it, and remove the cupping glass; and again apply the flax as before, and repeat this often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping used for the disease of pleurisy, which is acute, there is no wick nor hole, and it is not filled with fire except when it is full of air, and it is placed on the member alone; and that is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	The uses of leeches are not filled with fire except in members where one cannot place cups due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as the toes or nose, and others similar. And the qualities of using them are that when you find leeches that are in clear, sweet waters without corruption, then take them; and put them in a vessel with sweet water until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their bellies. And then let them be veined and cupped, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the leeches on it. And when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cup, then put it there, for this is very useful afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.
