If this is not the case, then lift the joint thusly, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the joint bleeds too much after the body of the veins, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put on, until the blood is stanched; and if the blood is multiplied, then put on crushed vitriol or saltpetre, or similar things, until it is stanched; or you can place half-peeled broad beans on the joint, and leave them there until they absorb into the joint, now it will be stanched; and if more are needed, take others.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not want to stand out, then rub the joint with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until some blood comes out, and then place them on it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will absorb; and when you see that they fall off, sprinkle some powder made of aloe and ground celery seed, or ash, now they will stick.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is very necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the treatment of fractures and dislocations."
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that foolish physicians cast aside this chapter, having never seen any of the old books nor read a letter from them; and for this reason knowledge has been lost in our land, for I found no good one among them; and I know nothing except through the knowledge of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science therein, and by experiment and practice in my life; and I have briefly described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and at the end I have summarized it, and clearly shown the forms of instruments arranged as follows, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the contents of the words and chapters where wise men place their understanding and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or contusion occurs in anyone, you must quickly warn the patient on either side, if any other condition does not prevent it entirely, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid eating cold things, that is to say, cold foods, and meat of birds and hares, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not overfill oneself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you doubt heating an abscess or spreading matter in the limb; then let the patient return to his former regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with foods that cause good growth and are moistening, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pears, apples, cow's milk, eggs, fresh fish, and similar things."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this nourishment muscles grow back more quickly and the fracture heals faster;"
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot be fully reset or healed properly due to stiffness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children; but treat them gently, bind the broken bone with strong plaster, joining it together until it is as firm as before; do not cut away any of its point, and therefore it must be nourished with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"There are fractures that occur suddenly, like falling from a horse, and others that occur gradually, like the splitting of a feather for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with only a small crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own device and appropriate tool in healing, according to what the memory brings back to its place; and bone fracture is known by the twisted position of the limb, clearly apparent by touch, and heard when pressed by the hand; but if there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient feels little pain, then there is no fracture; however, it may have a twist, crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move him by hand, but apply the medicines that come later and then gently immobilize him."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break which goes into a tree, and are the two parts dislocated, it is necessary to set them together evenly before the wound closes. And if the wound closes quickly, let it be for some days until the wound heals; then set it evenly at the joint where you can move it easily and know that the restoration of this one is easier than those with fractures. Then hold it steady as is appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it from two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or use your hand for small members, or use two strings, or one string and your hand. And place the member according to its natural shape so that when the broken parts of the member are aligned, join them with all strength and keep the additions in their places while you move it until they are healed, and make sure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join the two ends of the bone together in the best way.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"And feel it well with your hand if it seems not to be properly set: then raise it carefully and do not immobilize it too much nor press upon it as those do who cause hot inflammation and contracture in the limb through their improper handling, as we have often said."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, ensure that the patient does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning nor in any other manner; and make sure the limb is securely fastened so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when it feels no pain, then it is not set right, and you must position it so that it feels no pain; and make sure it is set straight so there are no twists when it is reset; the qualities of the broken limb depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that fractured limbs are diverse in size, length and shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	But for small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like, they must be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and calves, must be wrapped with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the entire limb equally on all sides so there is no slackness. Then bind it around with light pads, three or four turns depending on the limb, and hold your hand firmly on the entire bandage. Then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break can be slightly separated. And loosen the bandage bit by bit until you grasp a large part of the healthy area. Then take another bandage and wrap it around again over the broken area. Then return to the bottom of the break and tighten moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said above in the first binding. Then place between the bandages pads of linen or cloth until it is entirely even. Then bind all with a bandage from above and then place well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place a soothing, warm poultice that reduces inflammation, and leave it on for several days; then apply pressure with your thumbs, using something like half of a large cane stalk soaked in water, or wooden cloves, or palm leaves, shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the bandage placed on the fracture should be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be long enough for the limb's size or length. Then press on the bandages as you did with the first layer, then tie them using a medium-sized linen thread, not too thick nor too thin, like this: pull it tight first over the fracture; then tie it evenly, without leaving less than two finger widths between each bandage.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	"And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after the bandaging on healthy areas, place linen bandages or wool wadding underneath them so that it does not bruise."
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	"When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the skin is broken, I will speak about its treatment later on."
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	"And know that one should not bind all broken limbs with splints on the first day."
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	When the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply hot plasters immediately; after 5 or 7 days, according to your assessment of whether the inflammation is heating up. Here is the manner of the ancient emplastes for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: Take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with many eggs. Apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method of the restorative emplaster for fractures in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	"Another method for making a poultice that restores fractures, dislocations, and twists: Take of bdellium and ladanum and wild marjoram and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each 10 drams; aloes wood, 5 drams; aloeroot, 7 drams; grind them into a powder and mix it with many eggs. If the person's complexion is hot, use this poultice, for it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it is beneficial to many people."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of emplaster for twist: Take myrrh and nard, each 10 drachms; frankincense and aloe, each 9 drachms; acacia 6 drachms; bolic armenic 10 drachms. Grind well and mix with water or many eggs. Apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other manner to plaster joints and bones out of their places, and alleviate the pain occurring, and grind the bone, and break it: Take new linen, and moisten it in hot water and cooked oil, and place on the spot.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating heat from an abscess, and removes pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	"Another method for making a poultice that restores broken bones: Take dried fig leaves and dock leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner to plaster for the healing of bone fracture and to soften the remainder of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mullein, camomile flowers, violet petals, wheat flour – each one part; grind them and mix with wine. If the limb is hot, mix it with coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner to plaster stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess forms on the healing member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mullein, linseed, balm, melilot, senna, violet flowers and camomile flowers – each one part; grind them and mix with salt water, sweet water, or wine according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	"Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more. He says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard."
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	"And it seems to Galen that one should put dry and slightly warm things on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar substances, as we have said."
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	"Another method for making a poultice that is beneficial for wounds and pain: Take myrrh and the cut hair of men or feathers of birds, and violet leaves, each an equal part; grind them together and make a poultice with it."
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then wait a little while afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; thus do not let it heal for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and remove the bandage immediately, and lift away the plaster gently; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip in water, and apply it to the place until the itching stops, and the pain is eased. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage, until you are sure of a warm inflammation; and let the swelling of the limb subside, and the pain be removed, then begin again the gentle binding, and a little plaster, but do not bind too tightly as before; and continue gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen are all gone, and you need plaster and bandages again, then resume it, just as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If no improvement is seen in the limb from what we have said, it should not be dislocated until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; sometimes it can be left for up to 20 days, depending on what one sees, until the fracture is evident and the flesh approaches its proper alignment. Then it will hold more securely, and the bone will grow its flesh, as I said before. And if you see that the place dries out too much, know that nourishment cannot come there; then apply hot water compresses every time you dislocate it, doing this every third day, and slacken the bandage a little. By this method, nourishment will reach the limb quickly, and thus it will improve what foolish doctors do who reset the limb crookedly: that is wicked, and such actions are cowardly, and I see nothing else but leaving it and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures exist, and diverse figures, and the causes are distinguished: for there are fractures that are caused by blows from a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone down to the hip joint which is beneath the bone, just like breaking wood; and therefore this kind of fracture is called 'haichure'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion that embeds, splits, or crushes from a fall onto stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the bone tissue beneath the bone or is above it, and this wound can be large or small
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that enters the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, and therefore this fracture is called 'capillaire'; And if the wound is made either by striking with stone or by falling or by similar thing, and causes the piece of bone to enter inwards, and the place is raised like when goldsmiths strike on gold cups; then it enters between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their heads, like the head of a child; And all these kinds of fractures have small pieces that are dislodged like stars; And I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the displacement on them, by careful inspection, and by the corrupted flesh that is above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is recognized because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed on, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a fracture, pay attention to any accidents of illness, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, pallor, fever with chills, inflammation of the eyes, etc., in many conditions, he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accident and hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, especially in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you should hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupted and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If bone fragments reach the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part thusly. And it is necessary that you take hold of the patient's head, and uncover the bone in all ways possible, with great care over the shape of the wound. If blood flows or a large abscess forms during uncovering of the bone, help him as needed, and then fill the space with bandages moistened in rose oil. Let the wound rest until the large abscess subsides, and ensure there is no bleeding. Then begin removing the bone around it, which can be done in two ways.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	"And then I add another cut, greater than the first one."
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	"The second method is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron. And work lightly so that you do not injure the head."
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	"And if the bone is prominent and hard, then you must pierce around it before you administer cuts with trepanation, not so deep that they penetrate the soft bone, and each one should have a margin or circle on top to prevent the point from passing through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one fits in its place on the blade of the bone, so that you have trepanations for all testicles. And this is the form of the three kinds of trepanation:"
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	"The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place one trepanation on the bone and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone has been pierced; then remove the trepanation a little further away, and do this all around, then cut with scissors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as subtly and lightly as possible, so that you can remove the bone by hand or with any of the tools you have such as tweezers; and make sure that you do not touch the cerebellum or the medulla oblongata."
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And once you have pierced and trimmed the bone, it is necessary that you reset the remaining sharp edge of the bone with another tool resembling an incision blade, but this one must be thinner and more delicate than the others. If any small bones or fragments remain, remove them gently using the tools; then dress the wound with bandages and ointments as previously mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	"And the other way of operating is that which Galen recommends, which is safer; and he praises it very much, these are his words:"
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	"It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone where the fracture appears more openly, so that when you have exposed this part, then place beneath the head of this lenticular knife, of which here is the form:"
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too deeply on one side, for the flesh is thin on both sides so that the blade faces the bone; then strike lightly with a small hammer around the bone, but beware of the membrane underneath; if it adheres to the bone, remove it gently without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	"And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the dura mater, and the bone is only cut on top with small pieces, then it is necessary to remove this prominence and remove the scales with a fine razor that you should have in various quantities, so as to accommodate each place according to the operation and shape of the fracture."
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	"So remove first with large razors, and then with more delicate ones, and do not stop doing this until it is completely done."
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	"In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to adapt your action according to its direction; this is something that cannot be responded to by anyone who has dedicated their study to this art."
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is open, you must take one linen cloth according to its size, moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound. Then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this gently so as not to burden the wound, then apply a bandage above and do not tie too tightly, only enough to touch the wound itself. Leave it thus for one or two days until the inflammation has subsided, then remove it and apply medicines such as lily roots, vesce powder, frankincense powder, aloe, etc. Make these into powders and apply them to the wound, also administering mundification medicines without biting. Ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave oil or allow bowels to gather on it, for when bowels accumulate on the brain cloth, they corrupt and cause great harm to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	"Therefore be careful, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt."
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a blackness appears on the surface due to the medicine applied that has such virtue, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix it with one cloth, and put it on the surface; then treat as usual until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	"Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or only one is broken by itself, for these are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is struck or twisted, then it heals."
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must press your little finger or a needle into the nostril, and place the break evenly on your index finger and hold it there gently until the nostril regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain from your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	"And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you must insert a small rod with a rounded end into it."
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do likewise, and hasten to reset it on the first day if you can; but if not, after the seventh or tenth day when the swelling has subsided, then insert into the nose a wick made from linen cloths if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	"Or insert another one on the other side if there is a break there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill up the nostrils."
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers said that one must grease the tents with butter, changing each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary to grease them with a mixture of egg yolk and flour powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	"And sometimes feathers from a goose are inserted instead of bandages into the nostrils, with one soft cloth wrapped around them, and if the break is held in place, then let the patient blow gently through them; do what you see fit."
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	"And if inflammation appears in the nose while you are working on it, then insert there wax or cotton soaked in rose oil or a little bit of diacynthion."
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not form, apply a plaster with flour of sesame and powdered incense mixed with egg yolk. Then place light bandages on it without binding the nose. And if the break is small but fragmented into many pieces, extract them using appropriate instruments, then sew up the fissure and treat the surrounding flesh with appropriate ointments and plasters. If there are no internal wounds in the nose, cure the tents by inserting splints of lead until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only on one side, not completely broken into two pieces, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, place your left index finger in the patient's mouth and feel for it; if it is on the left jawbone, place your right index finger inside your mouth and gently press on the fracture from outside with your other hand until it aligns.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced by two fingers' width, you must apply traction forcefully until it is aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is displacement or fracture of teeth, thread them with gold, silver or silk thread. Then apply cerote on the broken jawbone and place a double cloth over it. Next, put on a well-made bandage or a piece of leather cut to size according to the length and width of the jawbone, and tie it securely behind the head. Tell the patient to rest and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the position changes, untie it on the third day and then reapply what was loosened. Then apply a plaster made from flour mixed with albumen or sesame flour, after removing the cerote. Next, place a light linen over the plaster. If the plaster dries and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; many times it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if swelling appears, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been lost. If so, use appropriate instruments to remove it carefully.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, widen it with a cautery according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these fragments, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is wide, and place one of the bandages suitable for this, to encourage flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	From the scalpel
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The scalpel has broken several times near the shoulder blade, and there are three types of breaks: either it is broken off in two places without any fragments, which is easiest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	The operation is as follows when there is no wound: you will need two assistants so that one can hold the scalpel which has been broken while the other extends the neck towards the part; then align the break between your hands so that the shape is correct and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round cloth or linen sponge under the patient's shoulder according to your needs; then lift the scalpel and grasp the sponge with your hand so that you can align the break correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the blade of the scalpel forward because it has gone in deep, then have the patient lie on their side with a pillow under their shoulder and place a small cushion underneath. Then have your assistant press down on the shoulder so that the bone of the blade is lifted up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the break with your hands and if it is displaced, you must cut upwards. Gently remove any fragments and if the bone cannot be realigned due to any obstruction, use one of the cutting instruments you have to remove the obstacle underneath the scalpel while protecting the tissues.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not raised, and let it be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and let it have two heads, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, like the pathway of the wound that you made when you handled the bones; and when you are assured of hot abscess, so cut the wound, and if the pathway is small, or you doubt hot abscess, then cover the wound with rags and cloths, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if granulation tissue is not present, soak a piece of gauze in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar, and apply it to the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strapping of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is that you place on the bone the plaster of mill dust and egg yolk, and put light dressings on top, and put a splint under the armpit if necessary; then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put a double cloth on the dressings and the plaster; then take a fine strip three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and put the strip on the fracture, and wind the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and tighten each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you see clearly that the strip does not move over the broken bone, then rewarm it every day, and when the swelling decreases, then loosen it; and make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder up; thus lighten the fracture of its weight by the lightening of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless some misfortune occurs, for up to twenty days; then recommence the plastering if it seems necessary, and tighten and leave it like that until it is restored; and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and in fewer for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Treatment of shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	**When the shoulder bone is broken or dislocated and not back in its place, you can only feel it by touching; so arrange it according to the shape of the break, and set it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can. Then put flour mixed with an egg on the place, and light bandages, and cover it with a double cloth. Then put a wide and thin plaster, a bit wider than the shoulder; and if there are any hairs under the plaster in some part of the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen bandages so that the plaster lies evenly; and then bind it all firmly with one great bandage, so that the plaster does not move from its place. Check the dressing every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it, and put the plaster back in its place if it has moved, and let the patient lie on his side. And the shoulder is healed in twenty days or in twenty-five. And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, for it's not bone that goes out easily.**
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of bone sticks out and is not beneath the heart, cut it off and apply the treatment for fracture of the collarbone as mentioned earlier to encourage granulation tissue formation.
de la brisure dou pis	Treatment of elbow fracture
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, it tilts downward, and the patient feels great pain and faintness, and quickly, and sometimes vomits blood, and the marrow appears through the broken bone.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration of it is that the patient lies often on their back, and places one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with their hands, and carefully puts them even in all ways they can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then places emplasters and compresses above the subtle point of salt or other light wood, and wraps it in one cloth, and ties it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turns the tie around to the back and tightens it evenly, and re-winds the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tightens it; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the emplaster, and addresses what has come there in ways of cures; then resets the emplaster, and tightens it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	de la brisure des costes
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs happens only in large places after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only because they are glarious; and one feels it well by examining the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you align the break evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a splint, and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is leaning inward, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung; and they have difficulty breathing, and cough up a lot of blood, and it is a serious condition, and the ancients used to put great effort into treating it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one should give him foods that swell the belly, to push back the break from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest abscesses come if they were not there before.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they are there, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	"And they said that one should place cupping glasses on the spot to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt whether the cupping glasses will draw out the excesses to the location due to the condition of weakness."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And they said that one should cover the spot with moistened wool in hot oil, and then place tents between the ribs to make the belt equal, after which it should be treated with pleurisy treatment, flesh, and medicine."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone pressing on the flesh, and there is doubt about the patient's condition, then it is necessary to cut above the location of the broken bone, and place an instrument beneath to protect the skin; then one should trim the bone and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and apply splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess begins to form, then place moist cloths soaked in rose oil on it and apply them to the spot; treat the area regularly as necessary for an abscess, and let him lie constantly on that side until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	"de la brisure dou col"
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	"No fracture ever comes to the bones of the neck, and hardly does it bend; and likewise to the spine of the back."
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if his hands are softened and swollen and numb, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that many are mortal in several conditions, and if he moves them and feels it well when they are pressed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if properly treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if his feet are softened, and if the accident has happened in his hands, and windy emission and excretion occur without control; and when he is continually laid on his belly, excretion occurs without control.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back and wants to saddle himself up, he cannot do so.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: therefore, do not labor over its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	"And if this accident does not happen to them, then the matter is lighter."
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	"And the treatment is that you should watch if there is hot inflammation, then put rose oil or goose grease on the spine until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, bind it with a bandage, and tell the patient to rest; and they should not sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are healed."
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	"And if any bone dislocates, one must compress on the chest; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound if it is large with one stitch, then treat it with ointment that penetrates the flesh until it heals; and if the socket of the bone is broken, which is called the 'socket of the cow,' put your left hand's pouch into it and place it level with the other hand with all your strength, then put on a plaster and a splint if necessary; then compress it, and if there is dislocated bone, open it up and remove it, and treat the wound until it heals."
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Here is the translation for "de la brisure de l’os de la hainche":
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If it happens that the bone of the temple is broken, and if this happens, there occurs a slight diminution to the head; and it makes one lean forward, and declines towards the parted side, and pain comes to the patient at the place where it is broken, and pricking, and swelling at what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you raise your hand up until you are above the break; and know what is the break and its shape; and if the break is at the head only, then set this break so that it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or declines inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of this break can be seen more easily.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it in its proper place, then put on the splint, then put a wooden or metal splint over it, and bind the break so that it does not move; and fill in the space under the ribs until the bandage is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their sound side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if any inflammation comes, do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as it should be, if there is no bad complication; and that is the manner of treatment.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the break of the shoulder blade
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder blade is that which is between the ribs and the head of the shoulder bone. And if it is broken, it should be restored in one of these two ways:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two joints together with two strings and hang them from above, and have the patient sit on one seat; then throw his broken arm onto the wood until it reaches the elbow, and place it in a curve of wood, then hang some heavy object or have the assistant pull it down; then put the break in line with your hands together so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to place the patient on their backrest and have them put their hand on their neck, then command two assistants to each take one end of the break with their hands—the first one taking the top part and the second one taking the bottom—and extend each one towards its side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then hold down the lien below the break and above it, extending each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, then you must put one lien in the middle under the saddle and the other towards the hip, under the break; and likewise if the break is towards the hip, it is necessary to place a lien gently, without labor, so that the break is even on its place and on the hip; then set the break evenly as it should be, and hold it steady so that no abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if there are gaps present, then do not tie it too tightly for at least 28 days, and put wet linen on it and rose oil until the inflammation is calmed; then tie it tight, and the method to tie it is as follows: place the splint on the break, then bring the arm close to the support and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; then put the bandage on and tie it tightly onto the support and arm so that the arm is in line with the stars, unless something prevents it or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving back into place, then use stars (splints) and put one larger and stronger than the others on top of the break with two fingers' width between each splint. Each splint should be large enough to extend three fingers past the break on either side; then tie them on as I described at the beginning of this chapter for the break, tying more tightly and without stretching too much.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the settling of the bones and the swelling as we have described, when you reset the broken limb, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave it tied for seven days as we have said; then examine each day every three days to ensure that no itching or inflammation comes to the place where the dressing cannot reach the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not untie it until after three days or more, and have the patient lie on his back, with his hands on his stomach. Put one cushion full of wool under the shoulder blade, ensuring it is evenly distributed, and watch every hour day and night to make sure the broken limb does not move or the ligaments soften. Then apply the address through the power of medicine, and give him the food we have mentioned before, making sure the food is initially subtle; when he begins to recover, then let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset forty days after the injury, at which point one must untie it and administer baths and ointment medicines to set them straight.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the restriction is ugly and swollen, then delay untying it for forty days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the two "fossicles", one of which is small and supports the wrist; the other is large and is located beneath it towards the little finger. Sometimes only the large fossicle breaks, or sometimes only the small one does, but both may also break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, restoration is easy, and healing is quick; but when large ones are broken, healing is difficult, and causes more pain than when they break together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be gently stretched out and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, it should be pulled harder; and stretched out on the cushion, with the pouch of the hand held higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the others, and the patient should cross their legs over themselves, with the cushion placed before them higher up so that the patient suffers no labor; then extend the minister's strong arm to the part below his hand or elbow, and another minister on the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then the physician should place it even according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are broken fragments in the fracture, then each should be placed back in its proper position; and if any fragment is too short to grasp with forceps, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off and remove the bone, as we have mentioned before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is also a wound from the breakage, I have spoken about it in the chapter on wounds specifically; so take care of it accordingly.
