Then remove the wax, and place the emplastre of powdered millstone with abundance of egg; then add the tiles, ensuring that the breaking tile is always stronger and a little wider than the others. Know that it should have six tiles on each arm in various arrangements: whether the breaker is in one of the bones or two; and tightened more above the breaker than elsewhere, and always less when moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the breaker be soft and moist, and not hard nor harsh; and let the threads with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the lien after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wash the limb with warm water until those itches are soothed; and let the limb rest not too tightly.

Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	"And if it is observed that the bandaging cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it thus for several days until the inflammation arrives, and then apply restraint."
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, then do not untie him for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if he around him, then let him place his hands on his neck, and keep his neck even, and guard against movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this dislocation is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and around both wrists, there are few fractures; it is mostly dislocation that occurs.

"And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, then the patient must sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of them correctly. Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient. Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the fracture is on the back of the hand, then you must place a splint above it and another below in the palm so that the hand is open and straight. Then bind it all around the hand, and make sure the binding between both wrists is secure."
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	"And if the fracture occurs on any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, then align it correctly and bind it with the palm. If you see fit, place a small straight splint to raise the fracture and keep it from moving. And if the fracture is on one of the other fingers, such as the index finger or another, align it and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together in one bandage, whichever is more useful; or place a splint on it like the thumb. Be wary of inflammation during restoration and take care to treat any heat that may occur, as I have said."
de la cuixe brisie	Regarding the fractured hip:
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The hip bone is often broken, which can be seen when it rotates forwards and backwards; and the restoration of this involves tying one bandage above the break and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	Then the patient lies on their face, then each of the ministers extends their bandage to their side evenly; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the dislocation is near the root of the thigh, then let one ligament be toward the knife handle, and the other ligament beneath the dislocation.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And likewise if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be near the knee, and let the extension be below; then the physician places the bone even with both hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then puts on the splint, and the bandage, so that no abscess appears.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot swelling, let it cool down first before returning to your task and care; the bandage should be done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the break a hard doubled bandage of two or three, and hold back the excesses, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the hip and the leg near the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread upwards; then wrap the bandage around the leg and hip, then place splints on the break, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and hip with soft cloths to ensure even pressure, then begin to tie firmly three or four times around the break; and as you go higher up the break, tie less tightly; then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and hip, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that it becomes loose, untie it and address whatever has come undone, as we have said many times before. And if there are any pieces of bone sticking out, remove them if possible; otherwise, split the space and draw them out. Then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone breaks in such a way that splints are placed on it, as in the case of the elbow and arm. Nevertheless, with this type of restoration, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is restored in about one month or a little less or a little more, depending on the differences in complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know this: In the cruciate ligament of the knee there is little breakage, but it tears often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is merely a crack or hole, and this happens with every wound, even without one. Everyone feels this.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by putting back in place what was around it until it fits as well as possible. Then put on the splint and add a round splint if necessary, tying it tightly enough. Then follow all the precautions that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as heat and inflammation; then apply whatever is appropriate for each case until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know this: The leg has two bones called by rights the "mustelz" and the "foscile", and its fracture is like that of the arm in every respect, with equal restoration. And if both bones are broken together, it twists the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, the foot turns inward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt and it is clearly visible; it turns towards the bottom.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply traction and set it evenly, then tie the splints evenly. But if the break is ugly with many pieces, make the traction lighter and gentler; adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, then take two strips of bark from the ash tree that will wrap around the leg on both sides and be as long as the leg from below the knee downwards; then wrap it in two layers with a bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left at this point, and thus it is good. And some also use one splint of wood the length of the leg and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly where there is a wound; and each day move the leg to see if there is any heat or other accident; and treat it until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not suffer fractures, but sometimes bones in the foot are broken and so are the toes; and there are many ways of treating these injuries.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones in the foot, and you see these bones sticking up above each other, then place your bad foot on the ground, as if it wanted to go forward, and then put your good foot on top of the broken bones, where they are raised up; then press down until they return to their proper places. Then apply splints and dressings, and place a small table with two hollowed-out legs under the instep of the foot; then strap it firmly around the foot, then wrap it in cloths and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, then set them back in place as we have said for the fingers of the hand. Then put a splint on the broken toe according to its length and make it a little wider; then place the table that I mentioned under the foot and strap it firmly around it. And if there are two or three or more toes broken, then put a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strap the table under the foot; and let them be placed at the top of the table so that they touch the underside of the foot well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have mentioned for other fractures, and treat each injury according to how it ought to be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the thumb bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit wide-legged, then lean her toward the back part, and have her held from behind. Then fill the cavity of the woman's nature with cotton, packing it in as thick as one's fist. Then lift the woman gently, little by little, causing the cotton to move until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bone will return with the fist. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has done so, put it back again, continuing this process for about seven days: thus the break will be restored. If you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube to its opening, insert the entire bladder into the nature, then blow into the tube forcefully until the bladder is inflated inside. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said regarding the thighbone; and these breakages are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice, and listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	But breaking means in many cases the direct way of restoration. So follow it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's neck and put it on the penis; then wrap cloths around it and leave it for three or four days, and it will soon be healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for anyone who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the arm or similar, to be healed now, according to the treatments that we have mentioned.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then rinse it with vinegar or nitre, and begin to restore the fracture at that same hour or day, provided that no fever ensues.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a fever ensues, then delay the restoration until the ninth day, until the inflammation is calmed, and do not attempt to touch it on the third or fourth day, lest you cause further harm.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is exposed above the heart, then it is necessary for you to put it back in place quickly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for putting it back in place with your hands, then use this iron instrument, which has seven or eight fingers of length and its width according to the size of the wound. And it is necessary for the doctor to shape three or four of them according to what is needed in each case of fracture; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your procedure. And have it pointed at the front and thicker at the middle towards the front like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'palainche', therefore the curved head must be placed on the visible bone end, pushing once until it returns and becomes even.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is small and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot put the bone back in place as we have said, then cut off the excess with an instrument suitable for this purpose, such as a chisel or a knife. Then smooth off the rough edges and small fragments that remain on the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So make sure it is in its natural position, then moisten a cloth in black setifical wine and cleanly apply it if it's summer; do not put cerate or any other oiled substance on the wound to prevent decay and corruption. Then apply bandages after resetting the bone, leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the surrounding skin according to the size of the wound. Be careful that the wound is not restricted with the fracture, as many foolish physicians have done, leading to death or corruption for the patient. Let the bandage be softer and gentler than usual for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that some misfortune may come of it, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then do not put on bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when after one or two days you see that the wound has begun to close, then remove what you have placed on it from all sides, and put on healing salve, such as tetrafarmacon salve and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	"And it is necessary that you wash the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is clean and healthy."
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	"And the limb must be positioned in such a way that the bowel moves down easily."
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	"And if many days pass and it does not heal but the bowel returns again, know that there are small bone fragments, so you must clean the wound with a cloth and remove all these unwanted pieces that cause this pain."
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears at the site, or some other kind of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the thighbone or shoulderbone and other similar large bones, do not pull it out, for many people die from this, but let it rot until after 20 or 30 days perhaps it will fall off by itself; then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	"of the bruises that come on the sore"
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	"We often see afterwards the condition of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and the sight of the limb's figure is unpleasant; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions."
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	"Therefore, beware if the bone is fresh: if the physician applies medicines that are astringent, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together and mix them with tincture of wine or with egg yolk or with garlic; and put them on the bone in poultices, and bind it well and do not remove it for several days; and then remove it, and begin again another one until the swelling is gone; or you can bind a well-made piece of lead onto it; because the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut off the excess above and make the apparent superf
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	"of the limb which becomes weak after the treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	"If the fracture of the bone is healed and afterwards the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings and nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of too much exercise; or because of too sudden movements, not at the right time; or because there was little blood in his body, so he is weak."
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	"And the cure is to make the sick person eat and make his body supple until blood is multiplied in him; and apply baths, and give him joy and pleasure; then put pitch on the limb so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and often rub it with warm water until nourishment reaches the limb; and finally return it to its natural figure."
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	"of the limb twisted after the healing"
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after being restored, and the broken bone becomes visible, and the form of the limb is unsightly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: thus do not believe the foolish who say one must break the limb again anew, many a foolish physician has done this in our land; and these works are blameworthy, and great evils come of them, sometimes even death. Nonetheless, if the joints and ligaments are fresh, they should be rinsed with hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as willow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make one soft plaster, such as diacylon well made, and take the mucilage of willow, and cook it with goose grease or sesame oil, and apply the plaster on. Or take ripe figs, crush them with fennel seed, and similar medicines that soften the adhesion.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation occurs due to prolonged and continuous rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And arrange for gentle movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is inveterate and hardened like stone, and it needs to be cut away with iron, then it must be cut down to the bone with a fine, light scalpel; and put care and skill into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint is displaced from its proper place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the sufferer feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, it must now be reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place swells up, and sometimes it is scarcely reset to its proper place; therefore, do not move the limb when it is swollen: many times this brings on spasms and other pains. Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled until the inflammation is appeased; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each limb as it comes into its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have arranged chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	Of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws are dislocated and they become slightly displaced from their position, which makes them softened a little; sometimes both of them are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, causing saliva to drip out of the mouth so that it cannot be held in, nor can the mouth be closed, and speech becomes tangled with the tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it returns by itself with more dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and whole, you must quickly reset it without delay. And do this in such a way that the assistants hold the patient's head, and the surgeon places one hand with a pouch on the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and let the other two hands remain free to provide balance; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the master will put it back in place until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jawbone is dislocated, even if both jaws are dislocated together, then apply hot water and oil so that they can move more easily; do not force them back into place, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are realigned evenly, and the patient closes his mouth without softening, then place moistened cloths made from rose oil and wax onto it, then bind it lightly with soft bindings; and have the patient sleep on their back, with both shoulders between two pillows so that they do not move either to the right or left, nor try to chew, but take only light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed. Then they may eat what they wish easily, without trying to open their mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is completely healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if both jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fever and chills will ensue, and sometimes diarrhea, and sometimes vomiting of bile alone.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these symptoms, then know that it is a loss [of life]; and many times the person to whom this happens dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	Jaw dislocations are treated using forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The jaw cannot be dislocated on the side towards its continuity with the ear, and sometimes it is dislocated backwards, which can be felt distinctly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, extending their arms; then press firmly with your palm against the place, and it will return; then place the emplaster and bandage, binding it tightly; and the shoulder toward the side cannot dislocate again; if it does dislocate once, reset it to its place as we have said; then place the emplaster and bandage, binding it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed. The same applies for resetting the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocates only in three ways: one is that it dislocates at the part of the socket below; and the second is at the part of the breastbone; and rarely does it dislocate above, which happens little; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder blade, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates below towards the socket, especially those who are fat, as it pops in quickly; those who have enough flesh, it pops only slightly and returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes in certain men there is injury or fracture, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with heat and swelling, and they believe that it has been dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it until you are certain; then begin the treatment
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are downwards towards the socket, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, which you will find manifest in their diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the socket touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their neck nor move with any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not concealed, for you can feel it manifestly; and this manner of dislocation is difficult to reset when it is recent, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the surgeon to lift the hand of the patient upwards, then place their fingers beneath the armpit and forcefully raise the joint upwards in its place, and the surgeon lifts the hand up and places it underneath it will quickly come back into place
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If dislocation does not occur as we have described most days afterward, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and let them be given a moisturizing and soothing plaster, such as a decoction of mallow, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let it be applied. Then have the patient lie on their back, and place under their shoulder blade an even pillow, not too soft nor too hard. Then the doctor places their heel on the pillow, gently lifts the head of the affected shoulder, and pulls the patient's hand. And another servant holds the patient's head so that it does not move down. If the shoulder comes back into place correctly, then reset it in this manner: Have present a man who is larger than the patient; have him stand upright against the side, and place his shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, and lift the shoulder blade upwards, so that the patient hangs from the arm; and another servant pulls the patient's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, hang something heavy on him, and the dislocation will return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reset is also done in another way: a long stick is placed upright in the ground, with its top level with the knee-cap and neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but softly wrapped in cloth, and the patient stands on one end of the wood; then stretch his hand downwards on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place. And if it still does not want to return despite all these things we have said, then perform this cure: take a stick two spans long and four fingers wide, with a round top for easy insertion deep under the buttock.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then place on the head of the patient a cloth dampened with water so that the wood does not burn him; then put it under his armpit; and extend his arm over the log; and tie the shoulder to the log, and the arm at the hand's elbow joint, then put the arm over one step of a ladder wide enough, and let the hand hang downwards, and leave the body hanging on the other side: The dislocation will now be reduced.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever way this may be, then you must put under the armpit a wad of wool equal in size; then place on the shoulder the emplastrum prepared with powder from the millstone, with incense and albumen of egg all around; then draw it under the armpit gradually, and turn the bandage over the emplastrum, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let it remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he consume little food until the member is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then consume more afterwards after five or six days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is removed from its place due to moisture that has come there or for another reason, then you must administer cauteries with three holes, as it is shown before in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and afterwards after twenty days the joint is still dislocated, and he cannot raise his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder has been cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be reduced to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the breast and the paps, or behind, is made by impulse and extension of hands, and another bandage is administered to it; and care must be taken until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing pain comes to the member and slowness in movement, then the sick person should take many baths until that pain is alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated forwards and returns forwards; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially forwards and backwards, and the dislocation has not been reduced, for one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, so you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder completely.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reduce it before swelling comes there, for if swelling comes there, then reduction will be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be reduced entirely, especially if it is behind; so this dislocation is worse than others, and is of greater pain, and sometimes death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is when it can be reduced in such a way that you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread apart, and place the joints of your fingers according to the neck around, above, and below, and push the joint into his palm together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is forwards, then it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and pushes the neck that is dislocated from the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and it is necessary that two ministers extend the arm, and two ministers hold it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, then wrap a doubled cloth long and wide around it; and when the physician has joined the joint with his hand, then anoint it with any oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly until it returns; and when it is in place, put dry plaster with eggwhite, and bind it tightly, and tie the arm to the neck of the sick one, and leave it for several days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, then untie the bandage and leave it alone; and if you see that the joint has not healed well, then recommence the compress and the bandage, and leave it on for several days until it is firmly set; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves again, then bathe and rub him gently, and press until it is relaxed; or put a poultice of greasy mutton fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, if you rub the joint temperately, then put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath again; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if necessary, put damp hot fern ashes mixed with butter on it, and bind it.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is easy to reduce, easier than other joints. Nevertheless, it should be reduced as quickly as possible in the very hour that it occurs, before the place becomes swollen or a hot swelling comes there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is thus: You place the invalid hand on a table, and extend your own hand, and the physician places it evenly, so that he puts his palm on the surface of the joint, and presses until it returns completely to its proper position; you must then observe whether it is properly in place. Then the patient places the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the physician places his hand on the surface of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. But if not, then press with soothing plasters or hot compresses until it remains there without moving again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if the patient cannot bear it and you cannot place it back in its proper position after several days, then the joint remains twisted. And it does not harm anything except that the hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything: know then that the nerve or artery has been cut. There is no other remedy but to cauterize nearby with fire.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then remove it and leave it so."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then apply warm water poultice, and rub it until it becomes flexible."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	"On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The hand's fingers sometimes dislocate on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or at the front; then they are out of place and you push the dislocation towards your pouched area until it returns. Then support the head of the finger, tilt it towards the part where it was dislocated; leave it for two days, then align it on the third day; and tie it with a bandage as we have said, release it on the fourth day and make it move, then retie the bandage tightly. Do this repeatedly until it is firm. Do the same if it dislocates at the front of the hand, following what you've done here until it's healed.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	"On the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back"
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	"If the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are several dislocations, then there is no remedy, for death quickly ensues."
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the evacuations happen without intent and cannot be held back, and many times certain limbs are weakened, such as both thighs or both arms, or sometimes the spine moves in three places; that which moves at the rear is called 'gilbositez': its treatment is to turn over if gilbositez has come from childhood: then there is no cure nor healing for all of it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ones spoke of methods of treatment with big words, but there is not always great benefit in all of them; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have made tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the chest in front, there is no heat [fever]; and also that which comes directly to both sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which comes properly to the back, as I say; and it is necessary that the patient be laid on his face in one even place, and have a support underneath him so that he does not get injured. Then drive one stake at the head into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie one rope around the thighs of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants know how to hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two stakes. And let them be well fastened, the stake as we have said, and the physician put his palms firmly on the spine until it returns [to its normal position].
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three spans in length, and place it under the skin, and let the patient lie on their side, and insert the head of the board under the skin, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician put his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do this on the turn that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you drive two stakes into the head of the patient's arm at one span apart, and two others towards the feet, with a handbreadth between each stake above and below; and let there be a hole in each stake where the joint turns, and let the stakes be firmly fixed in the ground so they do not move; and let there be one turning stake between each of the two main stakes, on which the joint turns, with two small stakes of a handbreadth long for turning the joint; and then tie the bandage that is among the assembly to the joint towards the head, and the other bandage towards the feet at the other joint, and each of the assistants turn their stake with all their might, and the master bring the spine into line as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even [the dislocation], then place a drying plaster with abundant egg, and then the splints, and then the plate of three ounces in length, which should press on the location of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine; then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and let the patient use gentle nourishment until they are healed; and if any problem arises at the end of the healing process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines along with the plate that we mentioned earlier; sometimes one also administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes out on the back spine, and one believes it to be dislocation; but this is the bone that appears, for which one should not presume: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	"Dislocations of the hip"
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder are dislocated only by dislocation, not as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; but mostly inside others, and little dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the diseased knee appears more prominent than the healthy one; and the diseased person cannot bend their knee in the fire; and the place that is swollen with heat near an abscess is where the hipbone comes.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one whom it happens outside is that this accident is opposite to those in front
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of one whom it happens in front is that his leg seems well put together; nevertheless, he cannot bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot do so, and retains his urine, and the ankle swells up, and when he walks, he leans on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of one whom it happens behind is that he cannot straighten or bend his knee, and this leg is twisted compared to the other; the ankle is softened, and the bone of the thigh is located below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this type of dislocation is that you should check if the dislocation is old, and it remains in its position without any care; and there should not be any pride [in the affected person].
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, you should hurry to put the joint back in place, both inside and outside, and move it to the right and left. Perhaps it will return [to its normal position], and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare the minister strongly, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or the lien where it is tied on the knee; and another minister stretches his hand above in such a way that he puts his hands underneath the patient's buttocks, then lifts him gently with a soft lien onto the hip; and another holds the head of the lien; and all extend upwards and downwards at once until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching applies to four types of dislocation. If the dislocation has returned [to its normal position], as we have said, that is good
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this does not work, then you must apply treatment according to its likeness. When the dislocation is at the hip, you must place the patient on his healthy side, then put the lien on the root of the hip and the place that is below the angle, then stretch the lien upwards towards the angle, and towards the thigh; then another minister takes the patient's arms, embraces the large bone of the sick hip, and stretches it out strongly: now it will return to its place. This method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	**And if thou canst not fasten it in this manner that we have said, then thou must bind the two feet of the patient together with a soft strong bandage on the two heels, and on the two knees, and let the limb of the sick be stretched out two spans longer than the other; then hang it on the head of a stake, and let there be two long arms above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the hip, and let another minister hang with the sick who embraces forcibly the hip, for now the joint returns hastily.**
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	**And when the dislocation is at the back, then let the sick lie as we have said in that who has gibbosity; and remove one bandage from the sick limb properly, and also from the foot; then put two stakes, one at the head and another at the feet, then stick one stake between the thighs of the sick in this manner; and have moist cloths around it so that it does not burn the sick, then let each minister extend towards him, and the doctor put his hand equally on the dislocation.**
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, then place upon [a] table, and press as we have said in the case of kyphosis; let the patient lie on their sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is anterior, then extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said, and let the doctor place his pain on being above the affected ankle joint, then press with his other hand below towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, do not extend the patient downwards nor raise them up from the ground, but let them lie as if the hip was dislocated at the back, as we have said concerning childbirth upon the two hips; and let them lie on their face, with the leg extended as we have said before, and press upon the joint at the table; and it will be set when the patient extends their legs, and they are even; then join the thighs, place the splint, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and let them rest for three or four days, then untie it and replace the splint; and if you see that they are even, then bind again as before, and leave it for three days; then untie it and let it go gently until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Chapter on dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	"The kneecap can dislocate in three ways: inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward."
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	**And the sign of this is that you command the patient to bend their leg towards their hip, and if it does not touch their hip, know that they are dislocated; and the treatment for all of these is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg as far as they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your thighs, then bend both sides of the knee strongly; and another assistant extends their foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they easily touch their leg to their hip lightly; and apply the plaster on top, and keep the leg pressed against the hip, tied together tightly for three or four days, then untie it; and do not let the patient walk until the limb is strengthened.**
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	**And if the limb is not completely healed, then administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of dislocation of the hip, until it is fully set.**
de la dislocation dou talon	Chapter on dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	"The heel can sometimes be wry and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward."
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.
